### Natural hazards {#Natural_hazards}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=15 "Edit section: Natural hazards")\]  
See also: [List of earthquakes in the Philippines](/wiki/List_of_earthquakes_in_the_Philippines "List of earthquakes in the Philippines")

[Swiss Re](/wiki/Swiss_Re "Swiss Re") ranked Manila as the second-riskiest capital city to live in, citing its exposure to natural hazards such as earthquakes, tsunamis, typhoons, floods, and landslides.^[\[18\]](#cite_note-Philippine_Daily_Inquirer-19)^ The seismically active [Marikina Valley Fault System](/wiki/Marikina_Valley_Fault_System "Marikina Valley Fault System") poses a threat of a large-scale earthquake with an estimated [magnitude](/wiki/Moment_magnitude_scale "Moment magnitude scale") of between 6 and 7, and as high as 7.6^[\[176\]](#cite_note-MVFSUSGS-178)^ to Metro Manila and nearby provinces.^[\[177\]](#cite_note-179)^ Manila has experienced several deadly earthquakes, notably those of [1645](/wiki/1645_Luzon_earthquake "1645 Luzon earthquake") and 1677, which destroyed the stone-and-brick medieval city.^[\[178\]](#cite_note-Earthquake-180)^ Architects during the Spanish colonial period used the [Earthquake Baroque](/wiki/Earthquake_Baroque "Earthquake Baroque") style to adapt to the region's frequent earthquakes.^[\[179\]](#cite_note-City-181)^{#cite_ref-City_181-0}

Manila experiences between five and seven typhoons each year.^[\[180\]](#cite_note-AOML_FAQ_B2-182)^ In 2009, [Typhoon Ketsana (Ondoy)](/wiki/Typhoon_Ketsana "Typhoon Ketsana") struck the Philippines, leading to one of the worst floods in Metro Manila and several provinces in Luzon with an estimated damages worth ₱11 billion ([US$](/wiki/United_States_dollar "United States dollar")237 million),^[\[181\]](#cite_note-Ondoy-183)^^[\[182\]](#cite_note-184)^ and caused 448 deaths in Metro Manila alone. Following the aftermath of Typhoon Ketsana, the city began to dredge its rivers and improve its drainage network.{#cite_ref-184}  

### Parks and green spaces {#Parks_and_green_spaces}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=16 "Edit section: Parks and green spaces")\]  
See also: [Manila Bay](/wiki/Manila_Bay "Manila Bay") and [List of parks in Metro Manila](/wiki/List_of_parks_in_Metro_Manila "List of parks in Metro Manila")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Manila_Lawton_Ermita_Arroceros_Forest_Park_Paths_11.jpg/220px-Manila_Lawton_Ermita_Arroceros_Forest_Park_Paths_11.jpg)](/wiki/File:Manila_Lawton_Ermita_Arroceros_Forest_Park_Paths_11.jpg) The [Arroceros Forest Park](/wiki/Arroceros_Forest_Park "Arroceros Forest Park") is considered as the "last lung of Manila".^[\[183\]](#cite_note-Inquirer-185)^

[Metro Manila](/wiki/Metro_Manila "Metro Manila") is situated in a variety of ecosystems including [upland forests](/wiki/Upland_forest "Upland forest"), [mangrove forests](/wiki/Mangrove_forest "Mangrove forest"), [mudflats](/wiki/Mudflat "Mudflat"), sandy beaches, [sea grass meadows](/wiki/Seagrass_meadow "Seagrass meadow") and [coral reefs](/wiki/Coral_reef "Coral reef"). Metro Manila is home to urban parks, nature parks, plazas, nature reserves, and an arboretum. However, according to the Asian Green City Index, in 2007 Manila contained only an average of 4.5 square meters (48 sq ft) of green space per person, well below the index average of 39 square meters (420 sq ft)^[\[184\]](#cite_note-186)^ and below the [World Health Organization](/wiki/World_Health_Organization "World Health Organization") (WHO) recommended minimum of 9 square meters (97 sq ft) per person.^[\[185\]](#cite_note-187)^^[\[186\]](#cite_note-188)^{#cite_ref-188}

The [Arroceros Forest Park](/wiki/Arroceros_Forest_Park "Arroceros Forest Park") is a 2.2-hectare (5.4-acre) [nature park](/wiki/Nature_park "Nature park") situated in the heart of downtown Manila along the south bank of the [Pasig River](/wiki/Pasig_River "Pasig River"). Considered as the "last lung of Manila", the park was professionally planned in 1993 with its [secondary growth forest](/wiki/Secondary_growth_forest "Secondary growth forest") of 61 different native tree varieties and 8,000 ornamental plants providing a habitat for about 10 different bird species.^[\[187\]](#cite_note-phil-189)^{#cite_ref-phil_189-0}  

### Pollution {#Pollution}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: Pollution")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Manila_downtown_-_Binondo%2C_Quiapo%2C_Quezon_Bridge%2C_Pasig_River%2C_Arroceros_%28close-up%29_%28Manila%29%282018-02-07%29.jpg/220px-Manila_downtown_-_Binondo%2C_Quiapo%2C_Quezon_Bridge%2C_Pasig_River%2C_Arroceros_%28close-up%29_%28Manila%29%282018-02-07%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Manila_downtown_-_Binondo,_Quiapo,_Quezon_Bridge,_Pasig_River,_Arroceros_(close-up)_(Manila)(2018-02-07).jpg) [Smog](/wiki/Smog "Smog") in [Quiapo](/wiki/Quiapo,_Manila "Quiapo, Manila")-[Binondo](/wiki/Binondo "Binondo") area

[Air pollution](/wiki/Air_pollution "Air pollution") in Manila is due to industrial waste and automobiles.^[\[188\]](#cite_note-UNcyberbus-190)^^[\[189\]](#cite_note-191)^ Swiss firm [IQAir](/wiki/IQAir "IQAir") reported in December 2020 Manila experienced an average [PM2.5](/wiki/PM2.5 "PM2.5") concentration of 6.1×10^−6^ g/m^3^ (1.03×10^−8^ lb/cu yd), which is classed as "Good" according to recommendations made by the World Health Organization.^[\[190\]](#cite_note-192)^{#cite_ref-192}

According to a report in 2003, the Pasig River is one of the most-polluted rivers in the world in which 150 metric tons (150 long tons; 170 short tons) of domestic waste and 75 metric tons (74 long tons; 83 short tons) of industrial waste are dumped daily.^[\[191\]](#cite_note-193)^^\[*[needs update](/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items "Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers")*\]^ The city is the second-biggest waste producing metropolis in the country with 1,151.79 tons (7,500.07 cubic meters (264,862 cu ft)) per day, after Quezon City, which produces 1,386.84 tons (12,730.59 cubic meters (449,577 cu ft)) per day. Both cities were cited as having poor management in garbage collection and disposal.^[\[192\]](#cite_note-194)^{#cite_ref-194}

Rehabilitation efforts have resulted in the creation of parks along the riverside and stricter pollution controls.^[\[193\]](#cite_note-pianews-195)^^[\[194\]](#cite_note-196)^ In 2019, the [Department of Environment and Natural Resources](/wiki/Department_of_Environment_and_Natural_Resources "Department of Environment and Natural Resources") launched a rehabilitation program for Manila Bay that will be administered by different government agencies.^[\[195\]](#cite_note-197)^^[\[196\]](#cite_note-198)^{#cite_ref-198}  

Cityscape {#Cityscape}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: Cityscape")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Manila_Harbour_View_by_night_%28Thomas_Yie%29_-_Flickr.jpg/220px-Manila_Harbour_View_by_night_%28Thomas_Yie%29_-_Flickr.jpg)](/wiki/File:Manila_Harbour_View_by_night_(Thomas_Yie)_-_Flickr.jpg) The [Roxas Boulevard](/wiki/Roxas_Boulevard "Roxas Boulevard") skyline at night along [Manila Bay](/wiki/Manila_Bay "Manila Bay").

Manila is a [planned city](/wiki/New_town "New town"). In 1905, American architect and urban planner [Daniel Burnham](/wiki/Daniel_Burnham "Daniel Burnham") was commissioned to design the new capital.^[\[197\]](#cite_note-199)^ His design for the city was based on the [City Beautiful movement](/wiki/City_Beautiful_movement "City Beautiful movement"), which favored broad streets and avenues radiating out from rectangles. Manila is made up of fourteen city districts, according to Republic Act No. 409---the Revised Charter of the City of Manila---the basis of which officially sets the present-day boundary of the city.^[\[10\]](#cite_note-ra409-11)^ The districts [Santa Mesa](/wiki/Santa_Mesa "Santa Mesa"), which was partitioned from Sampaloc,^[\[198\]](#cite_note-200)^ and [San Andres](/wiki/San_Andres,_Manila "San Andres, Manila"), which was partitioned off from Santa Ana, were later created.{#cite_ref-200}

Manila's mix of [architectural styles](/wiki/Architectural_style "Architectural style") reflects its, and the Philippines', turbulent history. During World War II, Manila was razed to the ground by Japanese forces and the shelling of American forces.^[\[199\]](#cite_note-201)^^[\[200\]](#cite_note-202)^ After the war ended, rebuilding began and most of the historical buildings were reconstructed. Many of the historic churches and buildings in Intramuros, Manila's historic core, however, had been damaged beyond repair.^[\[201\]](#cite_note-Wernstedt-1967-203)^ Manila's current urban landscape is one of modern and contemporary architecture. Manila's historic sites under the entry of *The Walled City and Historic Monuments of Manila* is currently being proposed to the tentative list for future [UNESCO](/wiki/UNESCO "UNESCO") [World Heritage Site](/wiki/World_Heritage_Site "World Heritage Site") inscription.^[\[202\]](#cite_note-204)^{#cite_ref-204}  

### Architecture {#Architecture}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Architecture")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/GRMondala_Manila_Metropolitan_Theater.jpg/220px-GRMondala_Manila_Metropolitan_Theater.jpg)](/wiki/File:GRMondala_Manila_Metropolitan_Theater.jpg) The façade of the [Manila Metropolitan Theater](/wiki/Manila_Metropolitan_Theater "Manila Metropolitan Theater"), designed by Filipino architect [Juan M. Arellano](/wiki/Juan_M._Arellano "Juan M. Arellano") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Jones_Bridge_ML_PH_%28M._Onod_pic%29_-_Flickr.jpg/220px-Jones_Bridge_ML_PH_%28M._Onod_pic%29_-_Flickr.jpg)](/wiki/File:Jones_Bridge_ML_PH_(M._Onod_pic)_-_Flickr.jpg) [Jones Bridge](/wiki/Jones_Bridge "Jones Bridge") was redeveloped in 2019 to "restore" it to its near-original design using [Beaux-Arts architecture](/wiki/Beaux-Arts_architecture "Beaux-Arts architecture").

Manila is known for its eclectic mix of architecture that includes a wide range of styles spanning the city's historical and cultural periods. Its architectural styles reflect American, Spanish, Chinese, and Malay influences.^[\[203\]](#cite_note-205)^ Prominent Filipino architects including Antonio Toledo,^[\[204\]](#cite_note-206)^ Felipe Roxas,^[\[205\]](#cite_note-207)^ [Juan M. Arellano](/wiki/Juan_M._Arellano "Juan M. Arellano")^[\[206\]](#cite_note-208)^ and [Tomás Mapúa](/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_Map%C3%BAa "Tomás Mapúa") have designed significant buildings in Manila such as churches, government offices, theaters, mansions, schools, and universities.^[\[207\]](#cite_note-209)^{#cite_ref-209}

Manila is known for [its Art Deco theaters](/wiki/Art_Deco_theaters_of_Manila "Art Deco theaters of Manila"), some of which were designed by [Juan Nakpil](/wiki/Juan_Nakpil "Juan Nakpil") and [Pablo Antonio](/wiki/Pablo_Antonio "Pablo Antonio").^[\[208\]](#cite_note-210)^ The historic [Escolta Street](/wiki/Escolta_Street "Escolta Street") in Binondo has many buildings of [Neoclassical](/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture "Neoclassical architecture") and [Beaux-Arts](/wiki/Beaux-Arts_architecture "Beaux-Arts architecture") architectural styles, many of which were designed by prominent Filipino architects during the American colonial period between the 1920s and the late 1930s. Many architects, artists, historians, and heritage advocacy groups are campaigning for the restoration of Escolta Street, which was once the premier street of the Philippines.^[\[209\]](#cite_note-211)^{#cite_ref-211}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Luneta_Hotel.jpg/170px-Luneta_Hotel.jpg)](/wiki/File:Luneta_Hotel.jpg) The [Luneta Hotel](/wiki/Luneta_Hotel "Luneta Hotel"), an example of [French Renaissance architecture](/wiki/French_Renaissance_architecture "French Renaissance architecture") with Filipino stylized beaux art

Almost all of Manila's pre-war and Spanish colonial architecture was destroyed during the [1945 Battle of Manila](/wiki/Battle_of_Manila_(1945) "Battle of Manila (1945)") by intensive bombardment by the United States Air Force. Reconstruction took place afterward, replacing the destroyed historic Spanish-era buildings with modern ones, erasing much of the city's character. Some of the destroyed buildings, such as the Old Legislative Building (now the [National Museum of Fine Arts](/wiki/National_Museum_of_Fine_Arts_(Manila) "National Museum of Fine Arts (Manila)")), [Ayuntamiento de Manila](/wiki/Ayuntamiento_de_Manila "Ayuntamiento de Manila") (now the Bureau of the Treasury), and the under-construction [San Ignacio Church and Convent](/wiki/San_Ignacio_Church_(Manila) "San Ignacio Church (Manila)") (as the [Museo de Intramuros](/wiki/Museo_de_Intramuros "Museo de Intramuros")), have been reconstructed. There are plans to refurbish and restore several neglected historic buildings and places such as Plaza Del Carmen, [San Sebastian Church](/wiki/San_Sebastian_Church_(Manila) "San Sebastian Church (Manila)"), and the [NCCA Metropolitan Theater](/wiki/NCCA_Metropolitan_Theater "NCCA Metropolitan Theater"). Spanish-era shops and houses in the districts of [Binondo](/wiki/Binondo "Binondo"), [Quiapo](/wiki/Quiapo,_Manila "Quiapo, Manila"), and [San Nicolas](/wiki/San_Nicolas,_Manila "San Nicolas, Manila") are also planned to be restored as a part of a movement to restore the city to its pre-war state.^[\[210\]](#cite_note-212)^^[\[211\]](#cite_note-213)^{#cite_ref-213}

Because Manila is prone to earthquakes, Spanish colonial architects invented a style called [Earthquake Baroque](/wiki/Earthquake_Baroque "Earthquake Baroque"), which churches and government buildings during the Spanish colonial period adopted.^[\[179\]](#cite_note-City-181)^ As a result, succeeding earthquakes of the 18th and 19th centuries barely affected Manila, although they periodically leveled the surrounding area. Modern buildings in and around Manila are designed or have been retrofitted to withstand an 8.2 magnitude quake in accordance with the country's building code.^[\[212\]](#cite_note-214)^{#cite_ref-214}  

Demographics {#Demographics}
----------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Demographics")\]
{#cite_ref-LWUA-PopulationData_219-0}

| 1948 |  983,906  | +5.20% |
| 1960 | 1,138,611 | +1.22% |
| 1970 | 1,330,788 | +1.57% |
| 1975 | 1,479,116 | +2.14% |
| 1980 | 1,630,485 | +1.97% |
| 1990 | 1,601,234 | −0.18% |
| 1995 | 1,654,761 | +0.62% |
| 2000 | 1,581,082 | −0.97% |
| 2007 | 1,660,714 | +0.68% |
| 2010 | 1,652,171 | −0.19% |
| 2015 | 1,780,148 | +1.43% |
| 2020 | 1,846,513 | +0.72% |
|------|-----------|--------|
| Source: [Philippine Statistics Authority](/wiki/Philippine_Statistics_Authority "Philippine Statistics Authority")^[\[213\]](#cite_note-PSA20–13-215)^^[\[214\]](#cite_note-PSA15–13-216)^^[\[215\]](#cite_note-NSO10–13-217)^^[\[216\]](#cite_note-NSO07-13-218)^^[\[217\]](#cite_note-LWUA-PopulationData-219)^ |||
[Population Census of Manila]

[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Manila_population_pyramid.svg/220px-Manila_population_pyramid.svg.png)](/wiki/File:Manila_population_pyramid.svg) Manila population pyramid in 2021 [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Binondo_Chinese_New_Year_Ongpin_Street_2024-02-10.jpg/220px-Binondo_Chinese_New_Year_Ongpin_Street_2024-02-10.jpg)](/wiki/File:Binondo_Chinese_New_Year_Ongpin_Street_2024-02-10.jpg) People flocking to the [Binondo Chinatown](/wiki/Binondo "Binondo") during [Chinese New Year](/wiki/Chinese_New_Year "Chinese New Year")

According to the [2020 Philippine census](/wiki/2020_Philippine_census "2020 Philippine census"), Manila has a population of 1,846,513 people, making it the [second-most-populous city](/wiki/List_of_cities_in_the_Philippines "List of cities in the Philippines") in the Philippines.^[\[218\]](#cite_note-PSA15–NCR-220)^ Manila is [the most-densely populated city](/wiki/List_of_cities_proper_by_population_density "List of cities proper by population density") in the world, with 41,515 inhabitants per km^2^ in 2015.^[\[6\]](#cite_note-PSApopden-7)^ District 6 is listed as the densest with 68,266 inhabitants per km^2^, followed by District 1 with 64,936 and District 2 with 64,710. District 5 is the least-densely populated area with 19,235.^[\[219\]](#cite_note-manilapop-221)^{#cite_ref-manilapop_221-0}

Manila has been presumed to be the Philippines' largest city since the establishment of a permanent Spanish settlement, and eventually became the political, commercial, and ecclesiastical capital of the country.^[\[220\]](#cite_note-222)^ Since colonial times, Manila has been the destination of peoples whose origins are as wide-ranging as India^[\[221\]](#cite_note-223)^ and Latin America.^[\[222\]](#cite_note-224)^ Practicing [forensic anthropology](/wiki/Forensic_anthropology "Forensic anthropology"), while exhuming cranial bones in several Philippine cemeteries, researcher Matthew C. Go estimated that 7% of the mean amount, among the samples exhumed, have attribution to European descent.^[\[223\]](#cite_note-225)^ Research work published in the Journal of Forensic Anthropology, collating contemporary Anthropological data show that the percentage of Filipino bodies who were sampled from the [University of the Philippines](/wiki/University_of_the_Philippines "University of the Philippines"), that is [phenotypically](/wiki/Phenotype "Phenotype") classified as Asian ([East](/wiki/East_Asian "East Asian"), [South](/wiki/South_Asian "South Asian") and [Southeast Asian](/wiki/Southeast_Asian "Southeast Asian")) is 72.7%, Hispanic (Spanish-Amerindian Mestizo, [Latin American](/wiki/Latin_American "Latin American"), and/or Spanish-Malay [Mestizo](/wiki/Mestizo "Mestizo")) is at 12.7%, Indigenous American ([Native American](/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas "Indigenous peoples of the Americas")) at 7.3%, African at 4.5%, and European at 2.7%.^[\[224\]](#cite_note-226)^ Between the 1860s and 1890s, in urban areas of the Philippines -- especially Manila -- according to burial statistics, as much as 3.3% of the population were pure European Spaniards and pure Chinese composed 9.9% of the city's populace. The Spanish-Filipino and Chinese-Filipino Mestizo populations also fluctuated, with the mixed Spanish-Filipinos composing 19% of Manila's population.^[\[60\]](#cite_note-Estadismo1-62)^^: 539^ Eventually, these non-native categories diminished because they were assimilated into the majority Austronesian Filipino population.^[\[225\]](#cite_note-227)^ During the Philippine Revolution, the term "Filipino" included people of any race born in the Philippines.^[\[226\]](#cite_note-228)^^[\[227\]](#cite_note-229)^ This explains the abrupt drop of the proportion of Chinese, Spanish, and Mestizo peoples across the country by the time of the first American census in 1903, as the foreign and mixed descended peoples identified solely as pure Filipinos.^[\[228\]](#cite_note-230)^ Manila's population dramatically increased since the 1903 census because people tended to move from rural areas to towns and cities. In the 1960 census, Manila became the first Philippine city to exceed one million people -- more than five times of its 1903 population. The city continued to grow until the population stabilized at 1.6 million and experienced alternating increases and decreases starting in the 1990 census year. This phenomenon may be attributed to the higher growth experienced by suburbs and the already-very-high population density of the city. As such, Manila exhibited a decreasing percentage share of the metropolitan population^[\[229\]](#cite_note-231)^ from 63% in the 1950s to 27.5%^[\[230\]](#cite_note-232)^ in 1980, and 13.8% in 2015. The much-larger [Quezon City](/wiki/Quezon_City "Quezon City") marginally surpassed the population of Manila in 1990 and by the 2015 census it already has 1.1 million more people. Nationally, the population of Manila was expected to be overtaken by cities with larger territories such as [Caloocan](/wiki/Caloocan "Caloocan") and [Davao City](/wiki/Davao_City "Davao City") by 2020.^[\[231\]](#cite_note-233)^ The vernacular language is [Filipino](/wiki/Filipino_language "Filipino language"), which is mostly based on the [Tagalog language](/wiki/Tagalog_language "Tagalog language") of the city and its surroundings, and this Manilan form of spoken Tagalog has become the *[lingua franca](/wiki/Lingua_franca "Lingua franca")* of the Philippines, having spread throughout the archipelago through mass media and entertainment. [English](/wiki/Philippine_English "Philippine English") is the language most widely used in education and business, and is in heavy everyday use throughout Metro Manila and the rest of the Philippines.{#cite_ref-233}

[Philippine Hokkien](/wiki/Philippine_Hokkien "Philippine Hokkien"), which is locally known as *Lan-nang-oe* , a variant of [Southern Min](/wiki/Southern_Min "Southern Min"), is mainly spoken by the city's [Chinese-Filipino](/wiki/Chinese-Filipino "Chinese-Filipino") community. According to data provided by the Bureau of Immigration, 3.12 million Chinese citizens arrived in the Philippines from January 2016 to May 2018.^[\[232\]](#cite_note-234)^{#cite_ref-234}  

### Crime {#Crime}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Crime")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/PNP_Policemen_%28Rizal_Park%2C_Manila%3B_2015-06-12%29.jpg/220px-PNP_Policemen_%28Rizal_Park%2C_Manila%3B_2015-06-12%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:PNP_Policemen_(Rizal_Park,_Manila;_2015-06-12).jpg) [Manila Police District](/wiki/Manila_Police_District "Manila Police District") officers in [Rizal Park](/wiki/Rizal_Park "Rizal Park").

Crime in Manila is concentrated in areas that are associated with poverty, drug abuse, and gangs. Crime in the city is also directly related to its changing demographics and unique criminal justice system. The [illegal drug trade](/wiki/Illegal_drug_trade_in_the_Philippines "Illegal drug trade in the Philippines") is a major problem of the city; in [Metro Manila](/wiki/Metro_Manila "Metro Manila") alone, 92% of the barangays were affected by illegal drugs in February 2015.^[\[233\]](#cite_note-rapplerdrugtrade-235)^{#cite_ref-rapplerdrugtrade_235-0}

From 2010 to 2015, Manila had the second-highest index crime rates in the Philippines, with 54,689 cases or an average of about 9,100 cases per year.^[\[234\]](#cite_note-236)^ By October 2017, [Manila Police District](/wiki/Manila_Police_District "Manila Police District") (MPD) reported a 38.7% decrease in index crimes from 5,474 cases in 2016 to 3,393 in 2017. MPD's crime-solution efficiency also improved; six-to-seven of every ten crimes were solved by the city police force.^[\[235\]](#cite_note-237)^ MPD was cited as the Best Police District in Metro Manila in 2017 for registering the highest crime-solution efficiency.^[\[236\]](#cite_note-238)^{#cite_ref-238}  

### Religion {#Religion}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Religion")\]  
‹ The [template](/wiki/Help:Template "Help:Template") *[Pie chart](/wiki/Template:Pie_chart "Template:Pie chart")* is being [considered for merging](/wiki/Wikipedia:Templates_for_discussion/Log/2025_January_30#Template:Pie_chart "Wikipedia:Templates for discussion/Log/2025 January 30"). ›  
Religion in Manila (circa 2010)^[\[237\]](#cite_note-RELIGION-239)^{#cite_ref-RELIGION_239-0}  
[Catholicism](/wiki/Catholic_Church "Catholic Church") (93.5%)  
[Iglesia ni Cristo](/wiki/Iglesia_ni_Cristo "Iglesia ni Cristo") (1.9%)  
[Protestantism](/wiki/Protestantism "Protestantism") (1.8%)  
[Buddhism](/wiki/Buddhism "Buddhism") (1.1%)  
Other (1.4%)  

#### Christianity {#Christianity}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Christianity")\]

As a result of [Spanish](/wiki/Culture_of_Spain "Culture of Spain") cultural influence, Manila is a predominantly [Christian](/wiki/Christianity_in_the_Philippines "Christianity in the Philippines") city. As of 2010^[\[update\]](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit)^, 93.5% of the population were [Roman Catholic](/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_the_Philippines "Catholic Church in the Philippines"), 1.9% were adherents of the [Iglesia ni Cristo](/wiki/Iglesia_ni_Cristo "Iglesia ni Cristo"), 1.8% followed various [Protestant](/wiki/Protestantism "Protestantism"), and 1.1% were [Buddhists](/wiki/Buddhism "Buddhism"). Members of [Islam](/wiki/Islam "Islam") and other religions make up the remaining 1.4% of the population.^[\[237\]](#cite_note-RELIGION-239)^{#cite_ref-RELIGION_239-1}

Manila is the seat of prominent Catholic churches and institutions. There are 113 Catholic churches within the city limits; 63 of which are considered major shrines, basilicas, or cathedrals.^[\[238\]](#cite_note-240)^ [Manila Cathedral](/wiki/Manila_Cathedral "Manila Cathedral"), the country's oldest established church, is the seat of the [Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Manila](/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Manila "Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Manila").^[\[239\]](#cite_note-wow-241)^ There are another three basilicas in the city; [Quiapo Church](/wiki/Quiapo_Church "Quiapo Church"), [Binondo Church](/wiki/Binondo_Church "Binondo Church"), and the [Minor Basilica of San Sebastián](/wiki/Basilica_of_San_Sebastian,_Manila "Basilica of San Sebastian, Manila").^[\[240\]](#cite_note-242)^[San Agustín Church](/wiki/San_Agustin_Church,_Manila "San Agustin Church, Manila") in Intramuros is a [UNESCO](/wiki/UNESCO "UNESCO") [World Heritage Site](/wiki/World_Heritage_Site "World Heritage Site").^[\[241\]](#cite_note-243)^{#cite_ref-243}

Several [Mainline Protestant](/wiki/Mainline_Protestant "Mainline Protestant") denominations are headquartered in the city. [St. Stephen's Parish](/wiki/St._Stephen%27s_Parish_(Manila) "St. Stephen's Parish (Manila)") [pro-cathedral](/wiki/Pro-cathedral "Pro-cathedral") in Santa Cruz district is the [see](/wiki/Episcopal_see "Episcopal see") of the [Episcopal Church in the Philippines](/wiki/Episcopal_Church_in_the_Philippines "Episcopal Church in the Philippines")' Diocese of Central Philippines, while on Taft Avenue are the [main cathedral and central offices](/wiki/Iglesia_Filipina_Independiente_National_Cathedral "Iglesia Filipina Independiente National Cathedral") of *[Iglesia Filipina Independiente](/wiki/Iglesia_Filipina_Independiente "Iglesia Filipina Independiente")* (also called the Aglipayan Church), a [nationalist church](/wiki/Christian_nationalism "Christian nationalism") that is a product of the [Philippine Revolution](/wiki/Philippine_Revolution "Philippine Revolution"). [The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints](/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints "The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints") (LDS Church) has a [temple within Manila](/wiki/Manila_Philippines_Temple "Manila Philippines Temple"), one of two operating LDS temples in the Philippines.

The indigenous [Iglesia ni Cristo](/wiki/Iglesia_ni_Cristo "Iglesia ni Cristo") has several locales (akin to parishes) in the city, including its first chapel, now [a museum](/wiki/Iglesia_ni_Cristo_Museum_(Santa_Ana,_Manila) "Iglesia ni Cristo Museum (Santa Ana, Manila)"), in Punta, Santa Ana.^[\[242\]](#cite_note-244)^ [Evangelical](/wiki/Evangelical_Christian "Evangelical Christian"), [Pentecostal](/wiki/Pentecostal "Pentecostal") and [Seventh-day Adventist](/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist "Seventh-day Adventist") denominations also thrive. The headquarters of the Philippine Bible Society is in Manila. The main campus of the [Cathedral of Praise](/wiki/Cathedral_of_Praise "Cathedral of Praise") is located on Taft Avenue. [Jesus Is Lord Church Worldwide](/wiki/Jesus_Is_Lord_Church_Worldwide "Jesus Is Lord Church Worldwide") has several branches and campuses in Manila.{#cite_ref-244}

Religious groups such as [Members Church of God International (MCGI)](/wiki/Members_Church_of_God_International "Members Church of God International"),^[\[243\]](#cite_note-245)^ Iglesia ni Cristo, Jesus Is Lord Church Worldwide, and the [El Shaddai movement](/wiki/El_Shaddai_(movement) "El Shaddai (movement)") celebrate their anniversaries at Quirino Grandstand, which is an open space in Rizal Park.^[\[244\]](#cite_note-246)^{#cite_ref-246}

  * [![Manila Cathedral is the seat of Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Manila.](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Allan_Jay_Quesada_-_Manila_Cathedral_001.jpg/240px-Allan_Jay_Quesada_-_Manila_Cathedral_001.jpg)](/wiki/File:Allan_Jay_Quesada_-_Manila_Cathedral_001.jpg "Manila Cathedral is the seat of Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Manila.")  
  [Manila Cathedral](/wiki/Manila_Cathedral "Manila Cathedral") is the seat of [Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Manila](/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Manila "Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Manila").
  * [![The Minor Basilica of San Sebastián is the only all-steel church in Asia.\[245\]](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/San_Sebastian_Church%2C_Quiapo%2C_Manila%2C_Dec_2023.jpg/239px-San_Sebastian_Church%2C_Quiapo%2C_Manila%2C_Dec_2023.jpg)](/wiki/File:San_Sebastian_Church,_Quiapo,_Manila,_Dec_2023.jpg "The Minor Basilica of San Sebastián is the only all-steel church in Asia.[245]")  
  The [Minor Basilica of San Sebastián](/wiki/Basilica_of_San_Sebastian,_Manila "Basilica of San Sebastian, Manila") is the only [all-steel](/wiki/Steel_building "Steel building") church in Asia.^[\[245\]](#cite_note-whl-247)^
  * [![San Agustín Church in Intramuros, a UNESCO World Heritage Site](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/San_Agustin_Church_Intramuros_2023-05-28.jpg/240px-San_Agustin_Church_Intramuros_2023-05-28.jpg)](/wiki/File:San_Agustin_Church_Intramuros_2023-05-28.jpg "San Agustín Church in Intramuros, a UNESCO World Heritage Site")  
  [San Agustín Church](/wiki/San_Agustin_Church,_Manila "San Agustin Church, Manila") in [Intramuros](/wiki/Intramuros "Intramuros"), a [UNESCO World Heritage Site](/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site "UNESCO World Heritage Site")
  * [![Binondo Church serves the Roman Catholic Chinese community.](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Binondo%2C_Manila_San_Nicolas_Heritage_Centre_47.jpg/240px-Binondo%2C_Manila_San_Nicolas_Heritage_Centre_47.jpg)](/wiki/File:Binondo,_Manila_San_Nicolas_Heritage_Centre_47.jpg "Binondo Church serves the Roman Catholic Chinese community.")  
  [Binondo Church](/wiki/Binondo_Church "Binondo Church") serves the Roman Catholic Chinese community.
  * [![Quiapo Church, home of the iconic Black Nazarene, whose Traslacion feast is celebrated every January 9](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Quiapo_Church_2024-05-31.jpg/240px-Quiapo_Church_2024-05-31.jpg)](/wiki/File:Quiapo_Church_2024-05-31.jpg "Quiapo Church, home of the iconic Black Nazarene, whose Traslacion feast is celebrated every January 9")  
  [Quiapo Church](/wiki/Quiapo_Church "Quiapo Church"), home of the iconic [Black Nazarene](/wiki/Black_Nazarene "Black Nazarene"), whose *Traslacion* feast is celebrated every January 9

#### Other faiths {#Other_faiths}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Other faiths")\]

Manila has many [Taoist](/wiki/Taoist "Taoist") and Buddhist temples like [Seng Guan Temple](/wiki/Seng_Guan_Temple "Seng Guan Temple") that serve the spiritual needs of the [Chinese Filipino](/wiki/Chinese_Filipino "Chinese Filipino") community.^[\[246\]](#cite_note-248)^ Quiapo has a "[Muslim](/wiki/Islam_in_the_Philippines "Islam in the Philippines") town" that includes the city's largest mosque [Masjid Al-Dahab](/wiki/Masjid_Al-Dahab "Masjid Al-Dahab").^[\[247\]](#cite_note-249)^ Members of the Indian expatriate community can worship at the large [Hindu](/wiki/Hinduism_in_the_Philippines "Hinduism in the Philippines") temple in the city or at the [Sikh](/wiki/Sikhism "Sikhism") [gurdwara](/wiki/Gurdwara "Gurdwara") on [United Nations Avenue](/wiki/United_Nations_Avenue "United Nations Avenue"). The [Baháʼí Faith](/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith "Baháʼí Faith")'s governing body in the Philippines the [National Spiritual Assembly](/wiki/Spiritual_Assembly "Spiritual Assembly") is headquartered near Manila's eastern boundary with Makati.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^{#cite_ref-249}  

Economy {#Economy}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Economy")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Intramuros%2C_Binondo-Quiapo_skyline_MH_%28Manila%3B_07-19-2024%29.jpg/220px-Intramuros%2C_Binondo-Quiapo_skyline_MH_%28Manila%3B_07-19-2024%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Intramuros,_Binondo-Quiapo_skyline_MH_(Manila;_07-19-2024).jpg) Skyline of [Binondo](/wiki/Binondo,_Manila "Binondo, Manila"), the central business district of the city of Manila.

Manila is a major center for commerce, banking and finance, retailing, transportation, tourism, real estate, [new media](/wiki/New_media "New media"), [traditional media](/wiki/Old_media "Old media"), advertising, legal services, accounting, insurance, theater, fashion, and the arts. Around 60,000 establishments operate in the city.^[\[248\]](#cite_note-250)^{#cite_ref-250}

The National Competitiveness Council of the Philippines, which annually publishes the Cities and Municipalities Competitiveness Index (CMCI), ranks the country's cities, municipalities, and provinces according to their economic dynamism, government efficiency, and infrastructure. According to the 2022 CMCI, Manila was the second-most-competitive [highly urbanized city](/wiki/Highly_urbanized_city "Highly urbanized city") in the Philippines.^[\[249\]](#cite_note-251)^ Manila held the title of the country's most-competitive city in 2015, and since then has been in the top three, denoting Manila is consistently one of the best place to live in and do business.^[\[250\]](#cite_note-252)^ The city has an estimated [GDP](/wiki/Gross_domestic_product "Gross domestic product") of ₱987.88 billion^[\[251\]](#cite_note-253)^ and is the 3rd largest economy of the [National Capital Region](/wiki/Metro_Manila "Metro Manila"), accounting for 15% of the region's total economy as of 2023.^[\[252\]](#cite_note-254)^{#cite_ref-254}

[Binondo](/wiki/Binondo "Binondo"), the oldest and one of the largest [Chinatowns](/wiki/Chinatown "Chinatown") in the world, was the center of commerce and business activities in the city. Numerous residential and office skyscrapers occupy its medieval streets. As of 2013, plans by the city government of Manila to turn the Chinatown area into a [business process outsourcing](/wiki/Business_process_outsourcing "Business process outsourcing") (BPO) hub were in progress; thirty unoccupied buildings had been already identified for conversion into BPO offices. Most of these buildings are on [Escolta Street](/wiki/Escolta_Street "Escolta Street"), Binondo.^[\[253\]](#cite_note-255)^{#cite_ref-255}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Port_of_Manila.jpg/220px-Port_of_Manila.jpg)](/wiki/File:Port_of_Manila.jpg) View of the [Manila International Container Terminal](/wiki/Port_of_Manila "Port of Manila"), the chief port of the Philippines

The [Port of Manila](/wiki/Port_of_Manila "Port of Manila") is the largest seaport in the Philippines and the main international shipping route into the country. The [Philippine Ports Authority](/wiki/Philippine_Ports_Authority "Philippine Ports Authority") oversees the operation and management of the country's ports. [International Container Terminal Services Inc.](/wiki/International_Container_Terminal_Services_Inc. "International Container Terminal Services Inc."), according to the [Asian Development Bank](/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank "Asian Development Bank"), is one of the top-five major maritime terminal operators in the world,^[\[254\]](#cite_note-pse-256)^^[\[255\]](#cite_note-forbes-257)^ and has its headquarters and main operations at the Port of Manila. Another port operator, Asian Terminal Incorporated, has its corporate office and main operations at [Manila South Harbor](/wiki/Manila_South_Harbor#Manila_South_Harbor "Manila South Harbor"), and its container depository is in [Santa Mesa](/wiki/Santa_Mesa,_Manila "Santa Mesa, Manila"). Manila is classified as a Medium-Port Megacity, using the Southampton system for port-city classification.^[\[256\]](#cite_note-258)^{#cite_ref-258}

Manufacturers within the city produce industrial-related products such as chemicals, textiles, clothing, electronic goods, food, beverages, and tobacco products. Local businesses process primary commodities for export, including rope, plywood, refined sugar, [copra](/wiki/Copra "Copra"), and coconut oil. The food-processing industry is one of the most-stable manufacturing sector in the city.^[\[257\]](#cite_note-259)^{#cite_ref-259}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/CCP_in_Roxas_Boulevard_SJasminum_48_BSP_Multi-storey_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-CCP_in_Roxas_Boulevard_SJasminum_48_BSP_Multi-storey_%28cropped%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:CCP_in_Roxas_Boulevard_SJasminum_48_BSP_Multi-storey_(cropped).jpg) *[Bangko Sentral ng Pilipinas](/wiki/Bangko_Sentral_ng_Pilipinas "Bangko Sentral ng Pilipinas")* headquarters

[Pandacan oil depot](/wiki/Pandacan_oil_depot "Pandacan oil depot") houses the storage facilities and distribution terminals of [Caltex Philippines](/wiki/Chevron_Corporation "Chevron Corporation"), [Pilipinas Shell](/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell "Royal Dutch Shell"), and [Petron Corporation](/wiki/Petron_Corporation "Petron Corporation"); the major players in the country's petroleum industry. The oil depot has been a subject of various concerns, including its environmental and health impact on the residents of Manila. The Supreme Court ordered the oil depot to be relocated outside the city by July 2015,^[\[258\]](#cite_note-260)^^[\[259\]](#cite_note-261)^ but it failed to meet this deadline. Most of the oil depot facility inside the 33-hectare (82-acre) compound were demolished,^[\[260\]](#cite_note-262)^ and plans have been made to convert it into a transport hub or food park.^[\[261\]](#cite_note-263)^{#cite_ref-263}

Manila is a major publishing center of the Philippines.^[\[262\]](#cite_note-encarta-264)^ *[Manila Bulletin](/wiki/Manila_Bulletin "Manila Bulletin")* , the Philippines' largest broadsheet newspaper by circulation, is headquartered in Intramuros.^[\[263\]](#cite_note-Manila_Bulletin-265)^ Other major publishing companies in the country *[The Manila Times](/wiki/The_Manila_Times "The Manila Times")* , *[The Philippine Star](/wiki/The_Philippine_Star "The Philippine Star")* , and *[Manila Standard Today](/wiki/Manila_Standard_Today "Manila Standard Today")* are headquartered in the Port Area. The *[Chinese Commercial News](/wiki/Chinese_Commercial_News "Chinese Commercial News")* , the Philippines' oldest existing Chinese-language newspaper, and the country's third-oldest newspaper,^[\[264\]](#cite_note-memorial-266)^ is headquartered in Binondo. [DWRK](/wiki/DWRK "DWRK") used to have its studio at the FEMS Tower 1 along [Osmeña Highway](/wiki/Osme%C3%B1a_Highway "Osmeña Highway") in [Malate](/wiki/Malate,_Manila "Malate, Manila") before transferring to the [MBC Building](/wiki/Manila_Broadcasting_Company "Manila Broadcasting Company") at the [CCP Complex](/wiki/CCP_Complex "CCP Complex") in 2008.^[\[265\]](#cite_note-267)^{#cite_ref-267}

Manila serves as the headquarters of the [Bangko Sentral ng Pilipinas](/wiki/Bangko_Sentral_ng_Pilipinas "Bangko Sentral ng Pilipinas"), which is located on [Roxas Boulevard](/wiki/Roxas_Boulevard "Roxas Boulevard").^[\[266\]](#cite_note-BSP-268)^ The [Landbank of the Philippines](/wiki/Landbank_of_the_Philippines "Landbank of the Philippines") and [Philippine Trust Company](/wiki/Philippine_Trust_Company "Philippine Trust Company") also have their headquarters in Manila. [Unilever Philippines](/wiki/Unilever "Unilever") used to have its corporate office on [United Nations Avenue](/wiki/United_Nations_Avenue "United Nations Avenue") in [Paco](/wiki/Paco,_Manila "Paco, Manila") before transferring to [Bonifacio Global City](/wiki/Bonifacio_Global_City "Bonifacio Global City") in 2016.^[\[267\]](#cite_note-Unilever_Phils-269)^ Vehicle manufacturer [Toyota](/wiki/Toyota "Toyota") also has its regional office on UN Avenue.{#cite_ref-Unilever_Phils_269-0}  

### Tourism {#Tourism}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Tourism")\]  
Main article: [Tourism in Metro Manila](/wiki/Tourism_in_Metro_Manila "Tourism in Metro Manila")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Manila_Cathedral_at_Noon.jpg/170px-Manila_Cathedral_at_Noon.jpg)](/wiki/File:Manila_Cathedral_at_Noon.jpg) The historic [Plaza Moriones](/wiki/Plaza_Moriones,_Intramuros "Plaza Moriones, Intramuros") with the [Manila Cathedral](/wiki/Manila_Cathedral "Manila Cathedral") in the background.

Manila welcomes over one million tourists each year.^[\[262\]](#cite_note-encarta-264)^ Major tourist destinations include the historic Walled City of [Intramuros](/wiki/Intramuros "Intramuros"), the [Cultural Center of the Philippines Complex](/wiki/Cultural_Center_of_the_Philippines_Complex "Cultural Center of the Philippines Complex"),^[\[note 1\]](#cite_note-Manila_Note_II-270)^ [Manila Ocean Park](/wiki/Manila_Ocean_Park "Manila Ocean Park"), Binondo (Chinatown), Ermita, [Malate](/wiki/Malate,_Manila "Malate, Manila"), [Manila Zoo](/wiki/Manila_Zoo "Manila Zoo"), the [National Museum Complex](/wiki/National_Museum_Complex_(Manila) "National Museum Complex (Manila)"), and [Rizal Park](/wiki/Rizal_Park "Rizal Park").^[\[268\]](#cite_note-271)^ Both the historic Walled City of Intramuros and Rizal Park were designated as flagship destinations and as tourism enterprise zones in the [Tourism Act of 2009](/wiki/List_of_Philippine_laws#2009_(9519–9999) "List of Philippine laws").^[\[269\]](#cite_note-TourismAct-272)^{#cite_ref-TourismAct_272-0}

Rizal Park, also known as Luneta Park, is a national park and the largest urban park in Asia.^[\[270\]](#cite_note-273)^ with an area of 58 hectares (140 acres),^[\[271\]](#cite_note-274)^ The park was constructed to honor of the country's national hero [José Rizal](/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Rizal "José Rizal"), who was executed by the Spaniards on charges of subversion. The flagpole west of the Rizal Monument is the [Kilometer Zero](/wiki/Kilometre_Zero "Kilometre Zero") marker for distances to locations across the country. The park is managed by the National Parks and Development Committee.^[\[272\]](#cite_note-275)^{#cite_ref-275}

The 0.67-square-kilometer (0.26 sq mi) Walled City of [Intramuros](/wiki/Intramuros "Intramuros") is the historic center of Manila. It is administered by the [Intramuros Administration](/wiki/Intramuros_Administration "Intramuros Administration"), an attached agency of the [Department of Tourism](/wiki/Department_of_Tourism_(Philippines) "Department of Tourism (Philippines)"). It contains [Manila Cathedral](/wiki/Manila_Cathedral "Manila Cathedral") and the 18th Century [San Agustin Church](/wiki/San_Agustin_Church_(Manila) "San Agustin Church (Manila)"), a UNESCO World Heritage Site. [Kalesa](/wiki/Kalesa "Kalesa") is a popular mode of transportation for tourists in Intramuros and nearby places including Binondo, Ermita and Rizal Park.^[\[273\]](#cite_note-276)^ Binondo, the oldest Chinatown in the world, was established in 1521^[\[274\]](#cite_note-277)^ and served as a hub of Chinese commerce before the Spaniards colonized the Philippines. Its main attractions are [Binondo Church](/wiki/Binondo_Church "Binondo Church"), Filipino-Chinese Friendship Arch, Seng Guan Buddhist Temple, and authentic Chinese restaurants.{#cite_ref-277}

Manila is designated as the country's leading destination for [medical tourism](/wiki/Medical_tourism "Medical tourism"), which is estimated to annually generate $1 billion in revenue.^[\[275\]](#cite_note-278)^ Lack of a progressive health system, inadequate infrastructure, and the unstable political environment are seen as hindrances to its growth.^[\[276\]](#cite_note-279)^{#cite_ref-279}  

### Shopping {#Shopping}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Shopping")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Old_Tutuban_Train_Station%2C_Manila%2C_Aug_2024.jpg/220px-Old_Tutuban_Train_Station%2C_Manila%2C_Aug_2024.jpg)](/wiki/File:Old_Tutuban_Train_Station,_Manila,_Aug_2024.jpg) The old [Tutuban Main Station](/wiki/Tutuban_Center "Tutuban Center") built in 1892, which is now converted to a shopping mall [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Divisoria_Shopping.jpg/220px-Divisoria_Shopping.jpg)](/wiki/File:Divisoria_Shopping.jpg) [Divisoria](/wiki/Divisoria "Divisoria") is a popular flea market for locals and tourists. Shown is the interior of [168 Shopping Mall](/wiki/168_Shopping_Mall "168 Shopping Mall").

Manila is regarded as one of the best shopping destinations in Asia.^[\[277\]](#cite_note-280)^^[\[278\]](#cite_note-281)^ Major shopping malls, department stores, markets, supermarkets, and bazaars are located within the city.{#cite_ref-281}

[Divisoria](/wiki/Divisoria "Divisoria") in Tondo has been locally described as a "shopping mecca" of Manila.^[\[279\]](#cite_note-282)^^[\[280\]](#cite_note-283)^ Shopping malls sell goods at bargain prices. Small vendors occupy several roads, causing pedestrian and vehicular traffic. A well-known landmark in Divisoria is the [Tutuban Center](/wiki/Tutuban_Center "Tutuban Center"), a large shopping mall that is a part of the [Philippine National Railways](/wiki/Philippine_National_Railways "Philippine National Railways")' [Main Station](/wiki/Tutuban_railway_station "Tutuban railway station"). It attracts 1 million people every month and is expected to add another 400,000 people upon the completion of the [LRT Line 2](/wiki/Manila_Light_Rail_Transit_System_Line_2 "Manila Light Rail Transit System Line 2") West Extension, making it Manila's busiest transfer station.^[\[281\]](#cite_note-284)^ Another "lifestyle mall" is [Lucky Chinatown](/wiki/Lucky_Chinatown "Lucky Chinatown"). There are almost 1 million shoppers in Divisoria according to the Manila Police District.^[\[282\]](#cite_note-285)^{#cite_ref-285}

Binondo, the oldest Chinatown in the world,^[\[52\]](#cite_note-en.radio86.com-54)^ is the city's center of commerce and trade for all types of businesses run by Filipino-Chinese merchants, with a wide variety of shops and restaurants. [Quiapo](/wiki/Quiapo,_Manila "Quiapo, Manila") is referred to as the "Old Downtown", where [tiangges](/wiki/Tiangge "Tiangge"), markets, boutique shops, music and electronics stores are common.^[\[283\]](#cite_note-286)^ Many department stores are on [Recto Avenue](/wiki/Recto_Avenue "Recto Avenue").{#cite_ref-286}

[Robinsons Place Manila](/wiki/Robinsons_Place_Manila "Robinsons Place Manila") is Manila's largest shopping mall.^[\[284\]](#cite_note-287)^ The mall was the second and the largest [Robinsons Malls](/wiki/Robinsons_Malls "Robinsons Malls") built. [SM Supermalls](/wiki/SM_Supermalls "SM Supermalls") operates the shopping malls SM City Manila and [SM City San Lazaro](/wiki/SM_City_San_Lazaro "SM City San Lazaro"). SM City Manila is located on the former site of YMCA Manila beside [Manila City Hall](/wiki/Manila_City_Hall "Manila City Hall") in [Ermita](/wiki/Ermita,_Manila "Ermita, Manila"), while SM City San Lazaro is built on the site of the former San Lazaro Hippodrome in [Santa Cruz](/wiki/Santa_Cruz,_Manila "Santa Cruz, Manila"). The building of the former Manila Royal Hotel in Quiapo, which is known for its revolving restaurant, is now the [SM Clearance Center](/wiki/SM_Quiapo "SM Quiapo") and was established in 1972.^[\[285\]](#cite_note-288)^ The site of the [first SM Department Store](/wiki/SM_Quiapo "SM Quiapo") is Carlos Palanca Sr. (formerly Echague) Street in [San Miguel](/wiki/San_Miguel,_Manila "San Miguel, Manila").^[\[286\]](#cite_note-289)^{#cite_ref-289}  

Culture {#Culture}
------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Culture")\]  

### Museums {#Museums}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Museums")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/National_Museum_of_Fine_Arts_%28Manila%2C_2024%29_%28digitally_altered_to_remove_Torre_de_Manila%29.jpg/220px-National_Museum_of_Fine_Arts_%28Manila%2C_2024%29_%28digitally_altered_to_remove_Torre_de_Manila%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:National_Museum_of_Fine_Arts_(Manila,_2024)_(digitally_altered_to_remove_Torre_de_Manila).jpg) The [National Museum of Fine Arts](/wiki/National_Museum_of_Fine_Arts_(Manila) "National Museum of Fine Arts (Manila)")

As the cultural center of the Philippines, Manila has a number of museums. The [National Museum Complex](/wiki/National_Museum_Complex_(Manila) "National Museum Complex (Manila)") of the [National Museum of the Philippines](/wiki/National_Museum_of_the_Philippines "National Museum of the Philippines"), located in Rizal Park, is composed of the [National Museum of Fine Arts](/wiki/National_Museum_of_Fine_Arts_(Manila) "National Museum of Fine Arts (Manila)"), the [National Museum of Anthropology](/wiki/National_Museum_of_Anthropology_(Manila) "National Museum of Anthropology (Manila)"), the [National Museum of Natural History](/wiki/National_Museum_of_Natural_History_(Manila) "National Museum of Natural History (Manila)"),^[\[287\]](#cite_note-290)^ and the [National Planetarium](/wiki/National_Planetarium_(Manila) "National Planetarium (Manila)"). *[Spoliarium](/wiki/Spoliarium "Spoliarium")* , a famous painting by [Juan Luna](/wiki/Juan_Luna "Juan Luna"), can be found in the complex.^[\[288\]](#cite_note-291)^{#cite_ref-291}

The city hosts the [National Library of the Philippines](/wiki/National_Library_of_the_Philippines "National Library of the Philippines"), a repository of the country's printed and recorded cultural heritage, and other literary and information resources.^[\[289\]](#cite_note-292)^^[\[290\]](#cite_note-293)^ The [National Historical Commission of the Philippines](/wiki/National_Historical_Commission_of_the_Philippines "National Historical Commission of the Philippines") maintains two history museums in the city, which are the [Museo ni Apolinario Mabini -- PUP](/wiki/Mabini_Shrine_(Manila) "Mabini Shrine (Manila)") and the [Museo ni Jose Rizal -- Fort Santiago](/wiki/Rizal_Shrine_(Intramuros) "Rizal Shrine (Intramuros)").^[\[291\]](#cite_note-294)^ Museums established or run by the [National Library](/wiki/National_Library_of_the_Philippines "National Library of the Philippines") and by educational institutions such asDLS-CSB Museum of Contemporary Art and Design,^[\[292\]](#cite_note-295)^ [UST Museum of Arts and Sciences](/wiki/UST_Museum_of_Arts_and_Sciences "UST Museum of Arts and Sciences"),^[\[293\]](#cite_note-296)^ and the [UP Museum of a History of Ideas](/wiki/University_of_the_Philippines_Museum_of_a_History_of_Ideas "University of the Philippines Museum of a History of Ideas") are located in the city.^[\[294\]](#cite_note-297)^{#cite_ref-297}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Museo_Nacional_de_Historia_Natural%2C_Manila%2C_Filipinas%2C_2023-08-26%2C_DD_46.jpg/220px-Museo_Nacional_de_Historia_Natural%2C_Manila%2C_Filipinas%2C_2023-08-26%2C_DD_46.jpg)](/wiki/File:Museo_Nacional_de_Historia_Natural,_Manila,_Filipinas,_2023-08-26,_DD_46.jpg) [National Museum of Natural History](/wiki/National_Museum_of_Natural_History_(Manila) "National Museum of Natural History (Manila)") at Agrifina Circle, [Rizal Park](/wiki/Rizal_Park "Rizal Park")

[Bahay Tsinoy](/wiki/Bahay_Tsinoy "Bahay Tsinoy"), one of Manila's prominent museums, documents the lives of Chinese people and their contributions to the history of the Philippines.^[\[295\]](#cite_note-298)^^[\[296\]](#cite_note-299)^ Intramuros Light and Sound Museum chronicles Filipinos' desire for freedom during [the revolution](/wiki/Philippine_Revolution "Philippine Revolution") under Rizal's leadership and other revolutionary leaders. The [Metropolitan Museum of Manila](/wiki/Metropolitan_Museum_of_Manila "Metropolitan Museum of Manila") houses modern and contemporary visual arts, and exhibits Filipino arts and [culture](/wiki/Culture_of_the_Philippines "Culture of the Philippines").^[\[297\]](#cite_note-300)^{#cite_ref-300}

Other museums in the city are the [Museo Pambata](/wiki/Museo_Pambata "Museo Pambata"),^[\[298\]](#cite_note-301)^ a children's museum;^[\[299\]](#cite_note-302)^ and Plaza San Luis, an outdoor heritage public museum that includes nine Spanish [Bahay na Bato](/wiki/Bahay_na_Bato "Bahay na Bato") houses.^[\[300\]](#cite_note-303)^ Ecclesiastical museums located in the city are the Parish of the Our Lady of the Abandoned in Santa Ana;^[\[301\]](#cite_note-304)^ [San Agustin Church Museum](/wiki/San_Agustin_Church_(Manila) "San Agustin Church (Manila)");^[\[302\]](#cite_note-305)^ and the [Museo de Intramuros](/wiki/Museo_de_Intramuros "Museo de Intramuros"), which houses the ecclesiastical art collection of the [Intramuros Administration](/wiki/Intramuros_Administration "Intramuros Administration") in the reconstructed [San Ignacio Church and Convent](/wiki/San_Ignacio_Church_(Manila) "San Ignacio Church (Manila)").^[\[303\]](#cite_note-306)^{#cite_ref-306}  

### Sports {#Sports}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Sports")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Rizal_Memorial_Football_Stadium_-_grandstand%2C_track_and_field_%28Malate%2C_Manila%3B_11-27-2019%29.jpg/220px-Rizal_Memorial_Football_Stadium_-_grandstand%2C_track_and_field_%28Malate%2C_Manila%3B_11-27-2019%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Rizal_Memorial_Football_Stadium_-_grandstand,_track_and_field_(Malate,_Manila;_11-27-2019).jpg) Ground view of the city-owned [Rizal Memorial Stadium](/wiki/Rizal_Memorial_Stadium "Rizal Memorial Stadium"), part of the [Rizal Memorial Sports Complex](/wiki/Rizal_Memorial_Sports_Complex "Rizal Memorial Sports Complex"). [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Basketball_in_Intramuros.jpg/220px-Basketball_in_Intramuros.jpg)](/wiki/File:Basketball_in_Intramuros.jpg) Children playing basketball at the ruins of [San Ignacio Church](/wiki/San_Ignacio_Church_(Manila) "San Ignacio Church (Manila)") in Intramuros

Sports in Manila have a long and distinguished history. The city's, and in general the country's, main sport is [basketball](/wiki/Basketball "Basketball"). Most barangays have a basketball court or a makeshift one, and court markings are frequently drawn on the streets. Larger barangays have covered courts where inter-barangay leagues are held every April to May. Manila's major sports venues include [Rizal Memorial Sports Complex](/wiki/Rizal_Memorial_Sports_Complex "Rizal Memorial Sports Complex") and [San Andres Gym](/w/index.php?title=San_Andres_Gym&action=edit&redlink=1 "San Andres Gym (page does not exist)"), the base of the now-defunct [Manila Metrostars](/wiki/Manila_Metrostars "Manila Metrostars").^[\[304\]](#cite_note-307)^ Rizal Memorial Sports Complex houses [a track and football stadium](/wiki/Rizal_Memorial_Track_and_Football_Stadium "Rizal Memorial Track and Football Stadium"), [a baseball stadium](/wiki/Rizal_Memorial_Baseball_Stadium "Rizal Memorial Baseball Stadium"), tennis courts, [Rizal Memorial Coliseum](/wiki/Rizal_Memorial_Coliseum "Rizal Memorial Coliseum"), and [Ninoy Aquino Stadium](/wiki/Ninoy_Aquino_Stadium "Ninoy Aquino Stadium"); the latter two are indoor arenas. The Rizal complex had hosted several multi-sport events, such as the [1954 Asian Games](/wiki/1954_Asian_Games "1954 Asian Games") and the [1934 Far Eastern Games](/wiki/1934_Far_Eastern_Games "1934 Far Eastern Games"). When the Philippines hosts the [Southeast Asian Games](/wiki/Southeast_Asian_Games "Southeast Asian Games"), most of the events are held at the complex but in the [2005 Games](/wiki/2005_Southeast_Asian_Games "2005 Southeast Asian Games"), most events were held elsewhere. The [1960 ABC Championship](/wiki/1960_ABC_Championship "1960 ABC Championship") and the [1973 ABC Championship](/wiki/1973_ABC_Championship "1973 ABC Championship"), forerunners of the [FIBA Asia Championship](/wiki/FIBA_Asia_Championship "FIBA Asia Championship"), were hosted at the memorial coliseum; the [national basketball team](/wiki/Philippines_men%27s_national_basketball_team "Philippines men's national basketball team") won both tournaments.^[\[305\]](#cite_note-308)^ The [1978 FIBA World Championship](/wiki/1978_FIBA_World_Championship "1978 FIBA World Championship") was held at the coliseum although the latter stages were held in the [Araneta Coliseum](/wiki/Araneta_Coliseum "Araneta Coliseum") in Quezon City.{#cite_ref-308}

Manila has several other well-known sports facilities such as [Enrique M. Razon Sports Center](/wiki/Enrique_M._Razon_Sports_Center "Enrique M. Razon Sports Center") and the [University of Santo Tomas Sports Complex](/wiki/University_of_Santo_Tomas_Sports_Complex "University of Santo Tomas Sports Complex"), both of which are private venues owned by a university; [collegiate sports](/wiki/Collegiate_sports "Collegiate sports") are also held in the city; the [University Athletic Association of the Philippines](/wiki/University_Athletic_Association_of_the_Philippines "University Athletic Association of the Philippines") and the [National Collegiate Athletic Association](/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association_(Philippines) "National Collegiate Athletic Association (Philippines)") basketball games held at Rizal Memorial Coliseum and Ninoy Aquino Stadium, although basketball events have been transferred to [San Juan](/wiki/San_Juan,_Metro_Manila "San Juan, Metro Manila")'s [Filoil Flying V Arena](/wiki/Filoil_Flying_V_Arena "Filoil Flying V Arena") and Araneta Coliseum in Quezon City. Other collegiate sports are still held at Rizal Memorial Sports Complex. Professional basketball, which has been mostly organized by corporate teams, also used to play at the city but the [Philippine Basketball Association](/wiki/Philippine_Basketball_Association "Philippine Basketball Association") now holds their games at Araneta Coliseum and [Cuneta Astrodome](/wiki/Cuneta_Astrodome "Cuneta Astrodome") at [Pasay](/wiki/Pasay "Pasay"); the now-defunct [Philippine Basketball League](/wiki/Philippine_Basketball_League "Philippine Basketball League") played some of their games, such as its [1995--96 Philippine Basketball League season](/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_Philippine_Basketball_League_season "1995–96 Philippine Basketball League season"), at Rizal Memorial Sports Complex.^[\[306\]](#cite_note-309)^{#cite_ref-309}

[Manila Metrostars](/wiki/Manila_Metrostars "Manila Metrostars") participated in the [Metropolitan Basketball Association](/wiki/Metropolitan_Basketball_Association "Metropolitan Basketball Association").^[\[307\]](#cite_note-310)^ The Metrostars, named after the [Metrostar Express](/wiki/Metrostar_Express "Metrostar Express") -- the brand name of the [Metro Manila MRT-3](/wiki/MRT_Line_3_(Metro_Manila) "MRT Line 3 (Metro Manila)"), which does not have stations in the city -- participated in its first three seasons and won the 1999 championship.^[\[308\]](#cite_note-311)^ The Metrostars later merged with the [Batangas Blades](/wiki/Batangas_Blades "Batangas Blades") and subsequently played in [Lipa, Batangas](/wiki/Lipa,_Batangas "Lipa, Batangas"). Almost twenty years later, [Manila Stars](/wiki/Manila_Stars "Manila Stars") participated in the [Maharlika Pilipinas Basketball League](/wiki/Maharlika_Pilipinas_Basketball_League "Maharlika Pilipinas Basketball League"), reaching the Northern Division Finals in 2019. Both teams played in the San Andres Sports Complex. Other teams that represented Manila but did not host games in the city are the [Manila Jeepney F.C.](/wiki/Manila_Jeepney_F.C. "Manila Jeepney F.C.") and [FC Meralco Manila](/wiki/Loyola_F.C. "Loyola F.C."). The city's government acknowledged Jeepney as Manila's representative in the [United Football League](/wiki/United_Football_League_(Philippines) "United Football League (Philippines)"). Meralco Manila played in the [Philippines Football League](/wiki/Philippines_Football_League "Philippines Football League") and designated Rizal Memorial Stadium as their home ground.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^{#cite_ref-311}

Manila's [rugby league](/wiki/Rugby_league "Rugby league") team [Manila Storm](/wiki/Manila_Storm "Manila Storm") trains at Rizal Park and plays matches at Southern Plains Field, [Calamba, Laguna](/wiki/Calamba,_Laguna "Calamba, Laguna"). Baseball was previously a widely played sport in the city but in 2022, Manila had the Philippines' only sizable baseball stadium, [Rizal Memorial Baseball Stadium](/wiki/Rizal_Memorial_Baseball_Stadium "Rizal Memorial Baseball Stadium"), which hosted games of the now-defunct [Baseball Philippines](/wiki/Baseball_Philippines "Baseball Philippines"); [Lou Gehrig](/wiki/Lou_Gehrig "Lou Gehrig") and [Babe Ruth](/wiki/Babe_Ruth "Babe Ruth") were the first players to score a [home run](/wiki/Home_run "Home run") at the stadium during their tour of the country on December 2, 1934.^[\[309\]](#cite_note-312)^ [Cue sports](/wiki/Cue_sports "Cue sports") are also popular in Manila; billiard halls are present in most barangays. The [2010 World Cup of Pool](/wiki/2010_World_Cup_of_Pool "2010 World Cup of Pool") was held at [Robinsons Place Manila](/wiki/Robinsons_Place_Manila "Robinsons Place Manila").^[\[310\]](#cite_note-313)^{#cite_ref-313}

[Rizal Memorial Track and Football Stadium](/wiki/Rizal_Memorial_Track_and_Football_Stadium "Rizal Memorial Track and Football Stadium") hosted the first [FIFA World Cup](/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup "FIFA World Cup") qualifier in decades when the [Philippines](/wiki/Philippines_national_football_team "Philippines national football team") hosted [Sri Lanka](/wiki/Sri_Lanka_national_basketball_team "Sri Lanka national basketball team") in July 2011. The stadium, which was previously unfit for international matches, had been renovated before the match.^[\[311\]](#cite_note-314)^ The stadium also hosted its first [rugby test](/wiki/Test_match_(rugby_union) "Test match (rugby union)") for the [2012 Asian Five Nations Division I](/wiki/2012_Asian_Five_Nations_division_tournaments "2012 Asian Five Nations division tournaments") tournaments.^[\[312\]](#cite_note-315)^{#cite_ref-315}  

### Festivals and holidays {#Festivals_and_holidays}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Festivals and holidays")\]  
Further information: [Public holidays in the Philippines](/wiki/Public_holidays_in_the_Philippines "Public holidays in the Philippines")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Feast_of_Black_Nazarene%2C_Quiapo%2C_Manila.JPG/220px-Feast_of_Black_Nazarene%2C_Quiapo%2C_Manila.JPG)](/wiki/File:Feast_of_Black_Nazarene,_Quiapo,_Manila.JPG) Catholic devotees during the [Feast of the Black Nazarene](/wiki/Black_Nazarene "Black Nazarene") (*Traslacíon*)

Manila celebrates civic and national holidays. Because most of the city's residents are Roman Catholic,^[\[313\]](#cite_note-316)^^[\[314\]](#cite_note-317)^ most of the festivals are religious in nature. Araw ng Maynila, which celebrates the city's founding on June 24, 1571 ^[\[315\]](#cite_note-318)^ by the Spanish *[conquistador](/wiki/Conquistador "Conquistador")* [Miguel López de Legazpi](/wiki/Miguel_L%C3%B3pez_de_Legazpi "Miguel López de Legazpi"), was first proclaimed by the city's vice mayor [Herminio A. Astorga](/wiki/Herminio_A._Astorga "Herminio A. Astorga") on June 24, 1962. It has been annually commemorated under the [patronage](/wiki/Patron_saint "Patron saint") of [John the Baptist](/wiki/John_the_Baptist "John the Baptist"), and has always been declared by the national government as a special, non-working holiday through presidential proclamations. Each of the city's 896 barangays also have their own festivities, which are guided by their own [patron saints](/wiki/Patron_saint "Patron saint").^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^{#cite_ref-318}

Manila also hosts the [procession of the Feast of the Black Nazarene](/wiki/Black_Nazarene "Black Nazarene") (*Traslacíon* ), which is held every January 9 and draws millions of Catholic followers.^[\[316\]](#cite_note-319)^ Other religious festivities held in Manila are the Feast of Santo Niño in Tondo and Pandacan, which is held on the third Sunday of January;^[\[317\]](#cite_note-320)^^[\[318\]](#cite_note-321)^ the Feast of *Nuestra Señora de los Desamparados de Manila* (Our Lady of the Abandoned), the patron saint of [Santa Ana](/wiki/Santa_Ana,_Manila "Santa Ana, Manila"), which is held every May 12;^[\[319\]](#cite_note-322)^ and the *[Flores de Mayo](/wiki/Flores_de_Mayo "Flores de Mayo")* .^[\[320\]](#cite_note-323)^ Non-religious holidays include [New Year's Day](/wiki/New_Year%27s_Day "New Year's Day"), [National Heroes' Day](/wiki/National_Heroes%27_Day "National Heroes' Day"), [Bonifacio Day](/wiki/Bonifacio_Day "Bonifacio Day"), and [Rizal Day](/wiki/Rizal_Day "Rizal Day").^[\[321\]](#cite_note-324)^{#cite_ref-324}  

Government {#Government}
------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Government")\]  

### Local government {#Local_government}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Local government")\]  
Main article: [Sangguniang Panglungsod](/wiki/Sangguniang_Panglungsod "Sangguniang Panglungsod")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Manila_City_Hall_%28Manila%3B_07-22-2020%29.jpg/220px-Manila_City_Hall_%28Manila%3B_07-22-2020%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Manila_City_Hall_(Manila;_07-22-2020).jpg) [Manila City Hall](/wiki/Manila_City_Hall "Manila City Hall"), the seat of city government [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Manila_Mayor_Lacuna_in_City_Council_inaugural_session.jpg/220px-Manila_Mayor_Lacuna_in_City_Council_inaugural_session.jpg)](/wiki/File:Manila_Mayor_Lacuna_in_City_Council_inaugural_session.jpg) The inaugural session of the 12th [Manila City Council](/wiki/Manila_City_Council "Manila City Council") at the city hall (2022)

Manila, which is officially known as the City of Manila, is the [national capital](/wiki/Capital_city "Capital city") of the Philippines and is classified as a special city according to its income,^[\[322\]](#cite_note-325)^^[\[323\]](#cite_note-326)^ and a [highly urbanized city](/wiki/Cities_of_the_Philippines#classification "Cities of the Philippines") (HUC). The [Mayor of Manila](/wiki/Mayor_of_Manila "Mayor of Manila") is the chief executive, and is assisted by the vice mayor and the 38-member [City Council](/wiki/Manila_City_Council "Manila City Council"), who are elected as representatives of the six councilor districts within the city, and the municipal presidents of the [Liga ng mga Barangay](/wiki/Liga_ng_mga_Barangay "Liga ng mga Barangay") and [Sangguniang Kabataan](/wiki/Sangguniang_Kabataan "Sangguniang Kabataan").^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^{#cite_ref-326}

The city has no control over [Intramuros](/wiki/Intramuros "Intramuros") and [Manila North Harbor](/wiki/Port_of_Manila "Port of Manila"). The historic Walled City is administered by the [Intramuros Administration](/wiki/Intramuros_Administration "Intramuros Administration") while Manila North Harbor is managed by the [Philippine Ports Authority](/wiki/Philippine_Ports_Authority "Philippine Ports Authority"). Both are national government agencies. The barangays that have jurisdictions over these places oversee the welfare of the city's constituents but cannot exercise their executive powers. Manila had a 12,971 personnel complement at the end of 2018.^[\[324\]](#cite_note-2019audit-327)^ Under the proposed form of [federalism in the Philippines](/wiki/Federalism_in_the_Philippines "Federalism in the Philippines"), Manila may no longer be the capital and Metro Manila may no longer be the seat of government; the committee has not yet decided on the federal capital and states they are open to other proposals.^[\[325\]](#cite_note-328)^^[\[326\]](#cite_note-329)^{#cite_ref-329}

As of May 2022, the Mayor of Manila is [Maria Shielah "Honey" Lacuna-Pangan](/wiki/Honey_Lacuna "Honey Lacuna"), daughter of former Manila vice mayor [Danilo Lacuna](/wiki/Danilo_Lacuna "Danilo Lacuna"). Lacuna is the city's first female mayor.^[\[327\]](#cite_note-330)^ The vice mayor is [Yul Servo](/wiki/Yul_Servo "Yul Servo"). The mayor and the vice mayor are limited to up-to three terms, each term lasting for three years. The city has an ordinance penalizing [cat-calling](/wiki/Street_harassment "Street harassment") since 2018, and is the second city in the Philippines to do so after Quezon City, which passed a similar ordinance in 2016.^[\[328\]](#cite_note-331)^ In 2017, the city government planned to revise the existing curfew ordinance since the Supreme Court declared it unconstitutional in August that year. Of the three cities reviewed by the Supreme Court; the City of Manila, [Navotas](/wiki/Navotas "Navotas"), and Quezon City; only the curfew ordinance of Quezon City was approved.^[\[329\]](#cite_note-332)^^[\[330\]](#cite_note-333)^{#cite_ref-333}  

### National government {#National_government}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: National government")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/20/Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace_%28local_img%29.jpg/220px-Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace_%28local_img%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace_(local_img).jpg) [Malacañang Palace](/wiki/Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace "Malacañang Palace"), the [official residence](/wiki/Official_residence "Official residence") and workplace of the [President of the Philippines](/wiki/President_of_the_Philippines "President of the Philippines").

Manila, being the seat of political power in the Philippines, has the headquarters of several national government offices. Planning for the city's role as the center of government started during the early years of [American colonization](/wiki/History_of_the_Philippines_(1898%E2%80%931946) "History of the Philippines (1898–1946)"), when the U.S. envisioned a well-designed city outside the walls of Intramuros, and chose Bagumbayan, a former town that is now Jose Rizal Park to become the center of government. A design commission was given to [Daniel Burnham](/wiki/Daniel_Burnham "Daniel Burnham") to create a master plan for the city patterned after [Washington, D.C.](/wiki/Washington,_D.C. "Washington, D.C.")^[\[331\]](#cite_note-Morley-2018-334)^ but the plans were abandoned under the Commonwealth Government of [Manuel L. Quezon](/wiki/Manuel_L._Quezon "Manuel L. Quezon").^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^ A new government center was to be built on the hills northeast of Manila, in what is now Quezon City. Several government agencies have set up their headquarters in Quezon City but several key government offices are still based in Manila. Many of the plans were substantially altered after the devastation of Manila during World War II and by subsequent administrations.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^{#cite_ref-Morley-2018_334-0}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Supreme_Court_of_the_Philippines.jpg/220px-Supreme_Court_of_the_Philippines.jpg)](/wiki/File:Supreme_Court_of_the_Philippines.jpg) Facade of the [Supreme Court of the Philippines](/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Philippines "Supreme Court of the Philippines").

As the nation's capital, Manila hosts the [Office of the President](/wiki/Office_of_the_President_of_the_Philippines "Office of the President of the Philippines") and the President's [official residence](/wiki/Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace "Malacañang Palace"). It also houses important government agencies and institutions such as the [Supreme Court](/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Philippines "Supreme Court of the Philippines"), the [Court of Appeals](/wiki/Philippine_Court_of_Appeals "Philippine Court of Appeals"), the [Bangko Sentral ng Pilipinas](/wiki/Bangko_Sentral_ng_Pilipinas "Bangko Sentral ng Pilipinas"), the [Departments](/wiki/Executive_Departments_of_the_Philippines "Executive Departments of the Philippines") of [Budget and Management](/wiki/Department_of_Budget_and_Management "Department of Budget and Management"), [Finance](/wiki/Department_of_Finance_(Philippines) "Department of Finance (Philippines)"), [Health](/wiki/Department_of_Health_(Philippines) "Department of Health (Philippines)"), [Justice](/wiki/Department_of_Justice_(Philippines) "Department of Justice (Philippines)"), [Labor and Employment](/wiki/Department_of_Labor_and_Employment_(Philippines) "Department of Labor and Employment (Philippines)"), and [Public Works and Highways](/wiki/Department_of_Public_Works_and_Highways "Department of Public Works and Highways"). Manila also hosts important national institutions such as the National Library, National Archives, [National Museum of the Philippines](/wiki/National_Museum_of_the_Philippines "National Museum of the Philippines"), and [Philippine General Hospital](/wiki/Philippine_General_Hospital "Philippine General Hospital").^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^. Other notable institutions based in Manila are the [National Commission for Culture and the Arts](/wiki/National_Commission_for_Culture_and_the_Arts "National Commission for Culture and the Arts"), [National Historical Commission](/wiki/National_Historical_Commission "National Historical Commission"), [Film Development Council of the Philippines](/wiki/Film_Development_Council_of_the_Philippines "Film Development Council of the Philippines"), and the [Cultural Center of the Philippines](/wiki/Cultural_Center_of_the_Philippines "Cultural Center of the Philippines").

Congress previously held office at the [Old Congress Building](/wiki/Old_Legislative_Building_(Manila) "Old Legislative Building (Manila)").^[\[332\]](#cite_note-335)^ In 1972, due to declaration of martial law, Congress was dissolved; its successor, the [unicameral](/wiki/Unicameral "Unicameral") [Batasang Pambansa](/wiki/Batasang_Pambansa "Batasang Pambansa"), held office at the new [Batasang Pambansa Complex](/wiki/Batasang_Pambansa_Complex "Batasang Pambansa Complex"). When a new [constitution](/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Philippines "Constitution of the Philippines") restored the [bicameral](/wiki/Bicameral "Bicameral") Congress, the House of Representatives stayed at the Batasang Pambansa Complex and the Senate remained at the Old Congress Building. In May 1997, the Senate transferred to a new building, which it shares with the [Government Service Insurance System](/wiki/Government_Service_Insurance_System "Government Service Insurance System") on reclaimed land at [Pasay](/wiki/Pasay "Pasay"). The [Supreme Court](/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Philippines "Supreme Court of the Philippines") was due to transfer to its new campus at [Bonifacio Global City](/wiki/Bonifacio_Global_City "Bonifacio Global City"), [Taguig](/wiki/Taguig "Taguig"), in 2019 but the move was postponed to a later year.^[\[333\]](#cite_note-336)^{#cite_ref-336}

In Congress, Manila has six representatives, one each from [its six congressional districts](/wiki/Legislative_districts_of_Manila "Legislative districts of Manila").^[\[334\]](#cite_note-337)^{#cite_ref-337}  

### Finance {#Finance}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Finance")\]

In the 2019 Annual Audit Report published by the [Commission on Audit](/wiki/Commission_on_Audit_(Philippines) "Commission on Audit (Philippines)"), the revenue of the City of Manila was ₱16.534 billion.^[\[324\]](#cite_note-2019audit-327)^ It is one of the cities with the highest tax collection and internal revenue allotment.^[\[335\]](#cite_note-338)^ For the 2019 fiscal year, the tax revenue collected by the city was ₱8.4 billion. The city's Internal Revenue Allotment (IRA) from the National Treasury was ₱2.94 billion, and the city's total assets were worth ₱63.4 billion in 2019.^[\[324\]](#cite_note-2019audit-327)^ The City of Manila has the highest budget allocation for healthcare of all the cities and municipalities in the Philippines; the city maintains the six district hospitals, 59 health centers and lying-in clinics, and healthcare programs.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^{#cite_ref-2019audit_327-2}  

Infrastructure {#Infrastructure}
--------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Infrastructure")\]  

### Housing {#Housing}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Housing")\]
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/WTMP_PhotoPhilia_D12_Smokey_Mountain_Housing.JPG/220px-WTMP_PhotoPhilia_D12_Smokey_Mountain_Housing.JPG)](/wiki/File:WTMP_PhotoPhilia_D12_Smokey_Mountain_Housing.JPG) [Smokey Mountain](/wiki/Smokey_Mountain "Smokey Mountain") Housing Project was built on a former landfill. Continuous development of housing buildings continues up to the present day.

Development of public housing in Manila began in the 1930s under U.S. rule; Americans had to deal with the problem of sanitation and concentration of settlers around business areas.^[\[336\]](#cite_note-339)^ Business codes and sanitation laws were implemented in the 1930s. During this period until the 1950s, new communities were opened for relocation. Among these were Projects 1--8 in Quezon City^[\[337\]](#cite_note-340)^ and the Vitas tenement houses in Tondo.^[\[338\]](#cite_note-341)^ In 1947, the government implemented a public housing policy that established the People's Homesite and Housing Corporation (PHHC).^[\[339\]](#cite_note-342)^ A few years later, it established a Slum Clearance Committee which, with the help of the PHHC, relocated thousands of families from Manila and Quezon City to Sapang Palay in [San Jose del Monte, Bulacan](/wiki/San_Jose_del_Monte,_Bulacan "San Jose del Monte, Bulacan") in the 1960s.^[\[340\]](#cite_note-343)^{#cite_ref-343}

In 2016, the national government completed several medium-rise houses for 300 Manila residents whose slum community was destroyed by a fire in 2011.^[\[341\]](#cite_note-344)^ As of 2019, the city government plans to retrofit dilapidated tenements within the city,^[\[342\]](#cite_note-345)^ and will construct new housing buildings for the city's informal settlers such as the 14-story Tondominium 1 and Tondomium 2 buildings, containing 42-square-meter (450 sq ft), two-bedroom units.
