The construction of these new in-city vertical housing projects was funded by a loan from the [Development Bank of the Philippines](/wiki/Development_Bank_of_the_Philippines "Development Bank of the Philippines") and the [Land Bank of the Philippines](/wiki/Land_Bank_of_the_Philippines "Land Bank of the Philippines").^[\[343\]](#cite_note-346)^^[\[344\]](#cite_note-347)^{#cite_ref-347}

Since 2019, the Manila City Government has initiated six housing projects: Tondominium 1 \& 2, Binondominium, Basecommunity, San Lazaro Residences, Pedro Gil Residences, and San Sebastian Residences.^[\[345\]](#cite_note-348)^^[\[346\]](#cite_note-349)^^[\[347\]](#cite_note-350)^{#cite_ref-350}  

### Transportation {#Transportation}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: Transportation")\]  
Main articles: [Transportation in Metro Manila](/wiki/Transportation_in_Metro_Manila "Transportation in Metro Manila"), [Rail transportation in Metro Manila](/wiki/Rail_transportation_in_Metro_Manila "Rail transportation in Metro Manila"), and [Major roads in Metro Manila](/wiki/Major_roads_in_Metro_Manila "Major roads in Metro Manila")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/WTMP_Pangkat_E-14-3.JPG/220px-WTMP_Pangkat_E-14-3.JPG)](/wiki/File:WTMP_Pangkat_E-14-3.JPG) [Jeepneys](/wiki/Jeepney "Jeepney") are one of the most popular modes of transportation in Manila. [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Line_2_Train_near_Pureza_Station_%28Santa_Mesa%2C_Manila%29%282018-02-22%29.jpg/220px-Line_2_Train_near_Pureza_Station_%28Santa_Mesa%2C_Manila%29%282018-02-22%29.jpg)](/wiki/File:Line_2_Train_near_Pureza_Station_(Santa_Mesa,_Manila)(2018-02-22).jpg) [Pureza station](/wiki/Pureza_station "Pureza station") of [LRT Line 2](/wiki/LRT_Line_2_(Metro_Manila) "LRT Line 2 (Metro Manila)") in [Santa Mesa](/wiki/Santa_Mesa "Santa Mesa") [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/LRT-1_Blumentritt_2011.jpg/220px-LRT-1_Blumentritt_2011.jpg)](/wiki/File:LRT-1_Blumentritt_2011.jpg) [Blumentritt Station](/wiki/Blumentritt_station_(Line_1) "Blumentritt station (Line 1)") of the [LRT Line 1](/wiki/LRT_Line_1_(Metro_Manila) "LRT Line 1 (Metro Manila)")

One of the best-known modes of transportation in Manila is the [jeepney](/wiki/Jeepney "Jeepney"), which were patterned after [U.S. Army jeeps](/wiki/Jeep#World_War_II_Jeeps "Jeep") and have been in use since the mid-to-late 1940s.^[\[348\]](#cite_note-351)^ The [Tamaraw FX](/wiki/Tamaraw_FX "Tamaraw FX"), the third generation of the [Toyota Kijang](/wiki/Toyota_Kijang "Toyota Kijang"), once directly competed with jeepneys and followed fixed routes for a set price. They were replaced by the [UV Express](/wiki/UV_Express "UV Express"). All types of public road transportation in Manila are privately owned and operated under government-issued franchises.^\[*[citation needed](/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")*\]^{#cite_ref-351}

On a for-hire basis, the city is served by [taxicabs](/wiki/Taxicab "Taxicab"), "[tricycles](/wiki/Motorized_tricycle_(Philippines) "Motorized tricycle (Philippines)")" -- motorcycles with sidecars---the Philippine version of the [auto rickshaw](/wiki/Auto_rickshaw "Auto rickshaw")), and "*trisikads* ", "*sikads* " or "*kuligligs* "; bicycles with sidecars, the Philippine version of [pedicabs](/wiki/Cycle_rickshaw "Cycle rickshaw")), which are popular In some areas, especially Divisoria. Spanish-era horse-drawn [calesas](/wiki/Calesa "Calesa") are a popular tourist attraction and mode of transportation in Binondo and Intramuros. Manila will phase out all gasoline-run tricycles and pedicabs, and replace them with electric tricycles (e-trikes), and plans to distribute 10,000 e-trikes to qualified tricycle drivers from the city.^[\[349\]](#cite_note-352)^^[\[350\]](#cite_note-353)^ By January 2018, the city has distributed e-trikes to a number of drivers and operators in Binondo, Ermita, [Malate](/wiki/Malate,_Manila "Malate, Manila"), and Santa Cruz.^[\[351\]](#cite_note-354)^{#cite_ref-354}

Manila is serviced by [LRT Line 1](/wiki/LRT_Line_1_(Metro_Manila) "LRT Line 1 (Metro Manila)") (LRT-1) and [Line 2](/wiki/LRT_Line_2_(Metro_Manila) "LRT Line 2 (Metro Manila)") (LRT-2), which form the [Manila Light Rail Transit System](/wiki/Manila_Light_Rail_Transit_System "Manila Light Rail Transit System"). Development of the light rail system began in the 1970s during the presidency of Ferdinand Marcos, when the LRT Line 1 was built, making it the first light-rail system in Southeast Asia. Despite its name, LRT-1 operates as a [light metro](/wiki/Light_metro "Light metro"), running on dedicated rights-of-way. LRT 2 operates as a full-metro, heavy rail system. As of 2015, these systems were undergoing a multi-billion-dollar expansion.^[\[352\]](#cite_note-10points-355)^ The LRT runs along the length of [Taft Avenue](/wiki/Taft_Avenue "Taft Avenue") (N170/R-2) and [Rizal Avenue](/wiki/Rizal_Avenue "Rizal Avenue") (N150/R-9), while LRT-2 runs along [Claro M. Recto Avenue](/wiki/Recto_Avenue "Recto Avenue") (N145/C-1) and [Ramon Magsaysay](/wiki/Magsaysay_Boulevard "Magsaysay Boulevard") Boulevard (N180/R-6) from Santa Cruz, through Quezon City, and to Masinag in [Antipolo](/wiki/Antipolo "Antipolo"), [Rizal](/wiki/Rizal_(province) "Rizal (province)").{#cite_ref-10points_355-0}
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/PNR_Santa_Mesa_Station_with_INKA_train_%28Manila%3B_02-01-2020%29_wiki.jpg/220px-PNR_Santa_Mesa_Station_with_INKA_train_%28Manila%3B_02-01-2020%29_wiki.jpg)](/wiki/File:PNR_Santa_Mesa_Station_with_INKA_train_(Manila;_02-01-2020)_wiki.jpg) A [PNR 8000 class](/wiki/PNR_8000_class "PNR 8000 class") at [Santa Mesa station](/wiki/Santa_Mesa_station "Santa Mesa station"), the fourth station southbound from [Tutuban station](/wiki/Tutuban_station "Tutuban station") terminus.

[Tutuban station](/wiki/Tutuban_station "Tutuban station"), the central terminal of the [Philippine National Railways](/wiki/Philippine_National_Railways "Philippine National Railways"), lies within Manila.^[\[353\]](#cite_note-356)^^[\[354\]](#cite_note-357)^ Within Metro Manila, one commuter railway is in operation. The line runs in a general north--south direction from Tutuban (Tondo) toward the province of [Laguna](/wiki/Laguna_(province) "Laguna (province)"). The Port of Manila, which is located in the western section of the city on Manila Bay, is the largest and chief seaport of the Philippines.^[\[355\]](#cite_note-358)^ The [Pasig River Ferry Service](/wiki/Pasig_River_Ferry_Service "Pasig River Ferry Service") is another form of transportation.^[\[356\]](#cite_note-359)^ The city is also served by [Ninoy Aquino International Airport](/wiki/Ninoy_Aquino_International_Airport "Ninoy Aquino International Airport"), the country's main international airport and domestic air hub.^[\[357\]](#cite_note-360)^{#cite_ref-360}

Trolleys, hand-made human-powered metal handcarts operated by "trolley boys", transport people along sections of the PNR lines. This is a popular means of transportation because it is low-cost -- roughly ₱10 or US$.20 per trip -- and avoids traffic. Many trolley boys are homeless and live alongside the railroad line, which is actively used by passenger trains, making collisions with passenger trains a consistent danger, although casualties are rare. The trolley rides are unofficial and unregulated but tolerated by authorities.^[\[358\]](#cite_note-361)^^[\[359\]](#cite_note-362)^^[\[360\]](#cite_note-363)^^[\[361\]](#cite_note-364)^{#cite_ref-364}

Satellite navigation company [TomTom](/wiki/TomTom "TomTom") ranked Manila as the second world's most-traffic-congested city in 2019.^[\[362\]](#cite_note-365)^ According to [Waze](/wiki/Waze "Waze")'s 2015 "Global Driver Satisfaction Index", Manila has the worst traffic worldwide.^[\[363\]](#cite_note-366)^ Manila is notorious for its frequent [traffic jams](/wiki/Traffic_jam "Traffic jam") and high densities.^[\[364\]](#cite_note-367)^ The government has undertaken several projects to alleviate the traffic in the city, some of which include the proposed construction of a new viaduct or underpass at the intersection of [España Boulevard](/wiki/Espa%C3%B1a_Boulevard "España Boulevard") and Lacson Avenue;^[\[365\]](#cite_note-368)^ the construction of [Skyway Stage 3](/wiki/Metro_Manila_Skyway#Stage_3 "Metro Manila Skyway"), [NLEX Connector](/wiki/NLEX_Connector "NLEX Connector"), and [Pasig River Expressway](/wiki/Pasig_River_Expressway "Pasig River Expressway"); the proposed LRT Line 2 West Extension Project from Recto Avenue to Pier 4 of Manila North Harbor;^[\[366\]](#cite_note-369)^ the proposed construction of the PNR east--west line through España Boulevard to Quezon City; and the expansion and widening of several national and local roads. These projects, however, had yet to make any meaningful impact by 2014, and the traffic jams and congestion continue.^[\[367\]](#cite_note-370)^{#cite_ref-370}

The government, under its 2014 [Metro Manila Dream Plan](/wiki/Metro_Manila_Dream_Plan "Metro Manila Dream Plan") aims to address these urban transport problems. The plan is a list of short-term priority projects and medium-to-long-term infrastructure projects that will last up to 2030.^[\[368\]](#cite_note-371)^^[\[369\]](#cite_note-372)^{#cite_ref-372}  

### Water and electricity {#Water_and_electricity}

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: Water and electricity")\]

Water services used to be provided by the [Metropolitan Waterworks and Sewerage System](/wiki/Metropolitan_Waterworks_and_Sewerage_System "Metropolitan Waterworks and Sewerage System") (MWSS), which served 30% of the city; most other sewage was directly dumped into storm drains, septic tanks, and open canals.^[\[370\]](#cite_note-373)^ MWSS was [privatized in 1997](/wiki/Water_privatization_in_Metro_Manila "Water privatization in Metro Manila"), which split the water concession into the east and west zones. [Maynilad Water Services](/wiki/Maynilad_Water_Services "Maynilad Water Services") took over the west zone, of which Manila is a part. As of 2001, Maynilad Water Services provides the supply and delivery of potable water, and sewerage system in Manila^[\[371\]](#cite_note-374)^ but does not serve the southeastern part of the city, which belongs to the east zone that is served by [Manila Water](/wiki/Manila_Water "Manila Water").^[\[372\]](#cite_note-375)^ Electricity services are provided by [Meralco](/wiki/Meralco "Meralco"), the sole electricity distributor in Metro Manila.^[\[373\]](#cite_note-376)^{#cite_ref-376}  

Healthcare {#Healthcare}
------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=40 "Edit section: Healthcare")\]  
See also: [List of hospitals in Metro Manila](/wiki/List_of_hospitals_in_Metro_Manila "List of hospitals in Metro Manila")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Ph-mm-manila-ermita-taft_ave.-philippine_general_hospital_%28up-pgh%29_%282014%29.JPG/220px-Ph-mm-manila-ermita-taft_ave.-philippine_general_hospital_%28up-pgh%29_%282014%29.JPG)](/wiki/File:Ph-mm-manila-ermita-taft_ave.-philippine_general_hospital_(up-pgh)_(2014).JPG) [Philippine General Hospital](/wiki/Philippine_General_Hospital "Philippine General Hospital"), established in 1910, is the largest modern tertiary hospital in the country.^[\[374\]](#cite_note-377)^

[Manila Health Department](/wiki/Manila_Health_Department "Manila Health Department") is responsible for the planning and implementation of healthcare programs provided by the city government. Manila Health Department operates 59 health centers and six city-run hospitals, which are free of charge for the city's constituents. The six public city-run hospitals are [Ospital ng Maynila Medical Center](/wiki/Ospital_ng_Maynila_Medical_Center "Ospital ng Maynila Medical Center"), Ospital ng Sampaloc, Gat Andres Bonifacio Memorial Medical Center, Ospital ng Tondo, [Santa Ana Hospital](/wiki/Santa_Ana_Hospital_(Manila) "Santa Ana Hospital (Manila)"), and Justice Jose Abad Santos General Hospital.^[\[375\]](#cite_note-378)^ [Philippine General Hospital](/wiki/Philippine_General_Hospital "Philippine General Hospital"), a tertiary state-owned hospital in Manila, is operated by the [University of the Philippines Manila](/wiki/University_of_the_Philippines_Manila "University of the Philippines Manila"). The city is planning to build an education, research, and hospital facility for [cleft lip and cleft palate](/wiki/Cleft_lip_and_cleft_palate "Cleft lip and cleft palate") patients,^[\[376\]](#cite_note-379)^^[\[377\]](#cite_note-380)^ and to establish the first children's surgical hospital in Southeast Asia.^[\[378\]](#cite_note-381)^{#cite_ref-381}

Private corporations also provide healthcare in Manila. Private hospitals that operate in the city are [Manila Doctors Hospital](/wiki/Manila_Doctors_Hospital "Manila Doctors Hospital"),^[\[379\]](#cite_note-382)^ [Chinese General Hospital and Medical Center](/wiki/Chinese_General_Hospital_and_Medical_Center "Chinese General Hospital and Medical Center"),^[\[380\]](#cite_note-383)^ [José R. Reyes Memorial Medical Center](/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_R._Reyes_Memorial_Medical_Center "José R. Reyes Memorial Medical Center"),^[\[381\]](#cite_note-384)^ [Metropolitan Medical Center](/wiki/Metropolitan_Medical_Center "Metropolitan Medical Center"),^[\[382\]](#cite_note-385)^ [Our Lady of Lourdes Hospital](/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Lourdes_Hospital_(Manila) "Our Lady of Lourdes Hospital (Manila)"),^[\[383\]](#cite_note-386)^ and the [University of Santo Tomas Hospital](/wiki/University_of_Santo_Tomas_Hospital "University of Santo Tomas Hospital").^[\[384\]](#cite_note-387)^{#cite_ref-387}

The [Department of Health](/wiki/Department_of_Health_(Philippines) "Department of Health (Philippines)") (DOH) has its main office in Manila^[\[385\]](#cite_note-388)^ and operates San Lazaro Hospital, a special referral tertiary hospital. DOH also operates [Dr. Jose Fabella Memorial Hospital](/wiki/Dr._Jose_Fabella_Memorial_Hospital "Dr. Jose Fabella Memorial Hospital"), [Jose R. Reyes Memorial Medical Center](/wiki/Jose_R._Reyes_Memorial_Medical_Center "Jose R. Reyes Memorial Medical Center"), and [Tondo Medical Center](/wiki/Tondo_Medical_Center "Tondo Medical Center").^[\[386\]](#cite_note-389)^ Manila is the home to the headquarters of the [World Health Organization](/wiki/World_Health_Organization "World Health Organization")'s Regional Office for the Western Pacific and Country Office for the Philippines.^[\[387\]](#cite_note-390)^{#cite_ref-390}

The city government provides free immunization programs for children, who are specifically targeted against hepatitis B, hemophilus influenza B pneumonia, diphtheria, tetanus, polio, measles, mumps, and rubella. As of 2016, 31,115 children aged one and below have been fully immunized.^[\[388\]](#cite_note-391)^ Manila Dialysis Center, which provides free services for the poor, has been cited by the United Nations Committee on Innovation, Competitiveness and Public-Private Partnerships as a model for public-private partnership (PPP) projects.^[\[389\]](#cite_note-392)^^[\[390\]](#cite_note-393)^ The dialysis facility was named Flora V. Valisno de Siojo Dialysis Center in 2019, and was inaugurated as the largest free dialysis facility in the Philippines. It has 91 dialysis machines, which can be expanded up to 100, matching the capabilities of the [National Kidney and Transplant Institute](/wiki/National_Kidney_and_Transplant_Institute "National Kidney and Transplant Institute") (NKTI).^[\[391\]](#cite_note-394)^^[\[392\]](#cite_note-395)^{#cite_ref-395}  

Education {#Education}
----------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Education")\]  
Main articles: [List of universities and colleges in Manila](/wiki/List_of_universities_and_colleges_in_Manila "List of universities and colleges in Manila") and [Division of City Schools--Manila](/w/index.php?title=Division_of_City_Schools%E2%80%93Manila&action=edit&redlink=1 "Division of City Schools–Manila (page does not exist)")
[![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Pamantasan_ng_Lungsod_ng_Maynila.jpg/220px-Pamantasan_ng_Lungsod_ng_Maynila.jpg)](/wiki/File:Pamantasan_ng_Lungsod_ng_Maynila.jpg) The campus of the [Pamantasan ng Lungsod ng Maynila](/wiki/Pamantasan_ng_Lungsod_ng_Maynila "Pamantasan ng Lungsod ng Maynila") and [Baluarte de San Diego](/wiki/Baluarte_de_San_Diego "Baluarte de San Diego") in Intramuros [![](//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/De_La_Salle_University_Manila_La_Salle_Hall_Night_Skyline_Taft_Avenue.jpg/220px-De_La_Salle_University_Manila_La_Salle_Hall_Night_Skyline_Taft_Avenue.jpg)](/wiki/File:De_La_Salle_University_Manila_La_Salle_Hall_Night_Skyline_Taft_Avenue.jpg) [De La Salle University](/wiki/De_La_Salle_University "De La Salle University") is a [Lasallian educational institution](/wiki/Lasallian_educational_institutions "Lasallian educational institutions") established in 1911.

Manila has been a center of education since the colonial period.^[\[393\]](#cite_note-Ricklefs-2010-396)^ The city has several Philippine universities and colleges, some of which are the county's oldest. The city's [University Belt](/wiki/University_Belt "University Belt") has a high concentration of colleges and universities, which are a short walking distance of each other. The University Belt is at the boundaries between [San Miguel](/wiki/San_Miguel,_Manila "San Miguel, Manila"), [Quiapo](/wiki/Quiapo,_Manila "Quiapo, Manila"), and [Sampaloc](/wiki/Sampaloc,_Manila "Sampaloc, Manila") districts, while other clusters colleges lie along the southern bank of the Pasig River -- mostly in Intramuros and Ermita districts; and at the southernmost part of [Malate](/wiki/Malate,_Manila "Malate, Manila") near the city limits.{#cite_ref-Ricklefs-2010_396-0}

The historic district Intramuros once housed the [University of Santo Tomas](/wiki/University_of_Santo_Tomas "University of Santo Tomas") (1611), [Colegio de San Juan de Letran](/wiki/Colegio_de_San_Juan_de_Letran "Colegio de San Juan de Letran") (1620), and [Ateneo de Manila University](/wiki/Ateneo_de_Manila_University "Ateneo de Manila University") (1859).^[\[393\]](#cite_note-Ricklefs-2010-396)^^[\[394\]](#cite_note-PACUOrg-MemberSchools-397)^ Only Colegio de San Juan de Letran remains at Intramuros; the University of Santo Tomas transferred to a new campus at Sampaloc in 1927 and Ateneo de Manila University relocated to Loyola Heights, Quezon City, in 1952. In the 20th century, new non-sectarian schools were built; [Mapúa University](/wiki/Map%C3%BAa_University "Mapúa University") (1925), [Lyceum of the Philippines University](/wiki/Lyceum_of_the_Philippines_University "Lyceum of the Philippines University") (1952), and [Pamantasan ng Lungsod ng Maynila](/wiki/Pamantasan_ng_Lungsod_ng_Maynila "Pamantasan ng Lungsod ng Maynila") (1965) -- which is owned and operated by the Manila city government.^[\[395\]](#cite_note-398)^^[\[396\]](#cite_note-399)^ The four schools in the district formed the [Intramuros Consortium](/wiki/Intramuros_Consortium "Intramuros Consortium"). Other notable universities in the city include [National University](/wiki/National_University_(Philippines) "National University (Philippines)") (1900), [San Beda University](/wiki/San_Beda_University "San Beda University") (1901), the only [Benedictine](/wiki/Benedictine "Benedictine") university in Asia, [De La Salle University](/wiki/De_La_Salle_University "De La Salle University") (1911), the largest of all [De La Salle University System](/wiki/De_La_Salle_University_System "De La Salle University System") of schools, [St. Paul University Manila](/wiki/St._Paul_University_Manila "St. Paul University Manila") (1912), one of the seven campuses comprising the [St. Paul University System](/wiki/St._Paul_University_System "St. Paul University System") of schools, [Far Eastern University](/wiki/Far_Eastern_University "Far Eastern University") (1928), and [Adamson University](/wiki/Adamson_University "Adamson University") (1939).{#cite_ref-399}

The [University of the Philippines](/wiki/University_of_the_Philippines "University of the Philippines") (1908), the country's main state university, was established in Ermita, Manila. It moved its central administrative offices from Manila to Diliman in 1949 and eventually made the original campus the [University of the Philippines Manila](/wiki/University_of_the_Philippines_Manila "University of the Philippines Manila"), the oldest of the constituent universities of the University of the Philippines System, and the center of health-sciences education in the country.^[\[397\]](#cite_note-400)^ Manila is also the site of the main campus of the [Polytechnic University of the Philippines](/wiki/Polytechnic_University_of_the_Philippines_Santa_Mesa "Polytechnic University of the Philippines Santa Mesa"), the largest university in the country in terms of student population.^[\[398\]](#cite_note-401)^{#cite_ref-401}

The city's three-tier public education system, the [Division of the City Schools of Manila](/w/index.php?title=Division_of_City_Schools%E2%80%93Manila&action=edit&redlink=1 "Division of City Schools–Manila (page does not exist)"), is a branch of the [Department of Education](/wiki/Department_of_Education_(Philippines) "Department of Education (Philippines)"). The division oversees 71 public elementary schools and 32 public high schools, all located within the city's territory, except for Rafael Palma Elementary School, which is situated in Barangay La Paz, [Makati](/wiki/Makati "Makati"), near the border with Manila.^[\[399\]](#cite_note-402)^ The city also contains [Manila Science High School](/wiki/Manila_Science_High_School "Manila Science High School"), a pilot science high school.^[\[400\]](#cite_note-:1-403)^{#cite_ref-:1_403-0}

International relations {#International_relations}
--------------------------------------------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=47 "Edit section: International relations")\]

Manila hosts the foreign embassies of the [United States](/wiki/Embassy_of_the_United_States,_Manila "Embassy of the United States, Manila")^[\[433\]](#cite_note-436)^ and Vietnam.^[\[434\]](#cite_note-437)^ Honorary consulates of Belize, Burkina Faso, Jordan, Nepal, Poland, Iceland, Paraguay, Thailand, and Tunisia are based in the city.^[\[435\]](#cite_note-DFAGovPH-ForeignConsulates-438)^{#cite_ref-DFAGovPH-ForeignConsulates_438-0}

Notes {#Notes}
--------------

\[[edit](/w/index.php?title=Manila&action=edit&section=50 "Edit section: Notes")\]  
1. **[\^](#cite_ref-41)** This was spurred by a locally found sacred image, i.e., a [Black Madonna](/wiki/Black_Madonna "Black Madonna") of unknown origin; one theory is that it is from Portuguese-Macau, another is that it is a Tantric goddess and this was worshiped by the natives in a Pagan-Hindu manner and had survived Islamic iconoclasm by the Sultanate of Brunei. This image was interpreted to be of Marian nature, and it was found during the Miguel de Legazpi expedition and eventually, a Mexican hermit built a chapel around that image.{#cite_note-41}
{#cite_note-41}  
1. **[\^](#cite_ref-Manila_Note_II_270-0)** The city limits was at Vicente Sotto Street. The rest of the place south of the street belongs to [Pasay](/wiki/Pasay "Pasay"). Buildings and structures in CCP that falls under the jurisdiction of Manila includes the National Theater.{#cite_note-Manila_Note_II-270}

51. **[\^](#cite_ref-53)** Barrows, David (2014). ["A History of the Philippines"](http://www.gutenberg.org/files/38269/38269-h/38269-h.htm#pb139). *Guttenburg Free Online E-books* . **1** : 179. Within the walls, there were some six hundred houses of a private nature, most of them built of stone and tile, and an equal number outside in the suburbs, or "arrabales", all occupied by Spaniards ("todos son vivienda y poblacion de los Españoles"). This gives some twelve hundred Spanish families or establishments, exclusive of the religious, who in Manila numbered at least one hundred and fifty, the garrison, at certain times, about four hundred trained Spanish soldiers who had seen service in Holland and the Low Countries, and the official classes.{#cite_note-53}

52. \^ [^***a***^](#cite_ref-en.radio86.com_54-0) [^***b***^](#cite_ref-en.radio86.com_54-1) Raitisoja, Geni [" Chinatown Manila: Oldest in the world"](http://en.radio86.com/travel/travel-destinations/chinatown-manila-oldest-world) [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20110402180844/http://en.radio86.com/travel/travel-destinations/chinatown-manila-oldest-world) April 2, 2011, at the [Wayback Machine](/wiki/Wayback_Machine "Wayback Machine"), *Tradio86.com*, July 8, 2006, accessed March 19, 2011.{#cite_note-en.radio86.com-54}
{#cite_note-en.radio86.com-54}
53. **[\^](#cite_ref-55)** "In 1637 the military force maintained in the islands consisted of one thousand seven hundred and two Spaniards and one hundred and forty Indians." \~*Memorial de D. Juan Grau y Monfalcon, Procurador General de las Islas Filipinas, Docs. Inéditos del Archivo de Indias, vi, p. 425.* "In 1787 the garrison at Manila consisted of one regiment of Mexicans comprising one thousand three hundred men, two artillery companies of eighty men each, three cavalry companies of fifty men each." *La Pérouse, ii, p. 368.*{#cite_note-55}
{#cite_note-55}
54. **[\^](#cite_ref-56)** (Page 10) Pérez, Marilola (2015). [*Cavite Chabacano Philippine Creole Spanish: Description and Typology*](https://web.archive.org/web/20210114232555/https://escholarship.org/content/qt6xj6f1jt/qt6xj6f1jt_noSplash_fd187448d1120e8904337fe47b42df2a.pdf) (PDF) (PhD). University of California, Berkeley. Archived from [the original](https://escholarship.org/uc/item/6xj6f1jt) on January 14, 2021. The galleon activities also attracted a great number of Mexican men that arrived from the Mexican Pacific coast as ships' crewmembers (Grant 2009: 230). Mexicans were administrators, priests and soldiers (guachinangos or hombres de pueblo) (Bernal 1964: 188) many though, integrated into the peasant society, even becoming tulisanes "bandits" who in the late 18th century "infested" Cavite and led peasant revolts (Medina 2002: 66). Meanwhile, in the Spanish garrisons, Spanish was used among administrators and priests. Nonetheless, there is not enough historical information on the social role of these men. In fact some of the few references point to a quick integration into the local society: "los hombres del pueblo, los soldados y marinos, anónimos, olvidados, absorbidos en su totalidad por la población Filipina." (Bernal 1964: 188). In addition to the Manila-Acapulco galleon, a complex commercial maritime system circulated European and Asian commodities including slaves. During the 17th century, Portuguese vessels traded with the ports of Manila and Cavite, even after the prohibition of 1644 (Seijas 2008: 21). Crucially, the commercial activities included the smuggling and trade of slaves: "from the Moluccas, and Malacca, and India... with the monsoon winds" carrying "clove spice, cinnamon, and pepper and black slaves, and Kafir \[slaves\]" (Antonio de Morga cf Seijas 2008: 21)." Though there is no data on the numbers of slaves in Cavite, the numbers in Manila suggest a significant fraction of the population had been brought in as slaves by the Portuguese vessels. By 1621, slaves in Manila numbered 1,970 out of a population of 6,110. This influx of slaves continued until late in the 17th century; according to contemporary cargo records in 1690, 200 slaves departed from Malacca to Manila (Seijas 2008: 21). Different ethnicities were favored for different labor; Africans were brought to work on the agricultural production, and skilled slaves from India served as caulkers and carpenters. {#cite_note-56}
{#cite_note-56}
55. **[\^](#cite_ref-57)** ["Jesuits In The Philippines (1581-1768)" Page 132](https://archive.org/stream/in.ernet.dli.2015.530346/2015.530346.jesuits-in_djvu.txt) "In 1591 there arrived in Manila a secular priest named Juan Fernandez de Leon. He had led a hermit's life in Mexico and planned to continue it in the Philippines. For this purpose he built himself a retreat near a wayside shrine just outside the city walls which was dedicated to Our Lady of Guidance, Nuestra Sehora de Guia. His hermitage later gave its name to the entire district, which is called Ermita to this day."{#cite_note-57}

222. **[\^](#cite_ref-224)** Barrows, David (2014). ["A History of the Philippines"](http://www.gutenberg.org/files/38269/38269-h/38269-h.htm#pb139). *Guttenburg Free Online E-books* . **1** : 229. Reforms under General Arandía.---The demoralization and misery with which Obando's rule closed were relieved somewhat by the capable government of Arandía, who succeeded him. Arandía was one of the few men of talent, energy, and integrity who stood at the head of affairs in these islands during two centuries. He reformed the greatly disorganized military force, establishing what was known as the "Regiment of the King," **made up very largely of Mexican soldiers**. He also formed a corps of artillerists composed of Filipinos. These were regular troops, who received from Arandía sufficient pay to enable them to live decently and like an army.{#cite_note-224}

223. **[\^](#cite_ref-225)** Go, Matthew C. (January 15, 2018). ["An Admixture Approach to Trihybrid Ancestry Variation in the Philippines with Implications for Forensic Anthropology"](https://www.researchgate.net/publication/329903258). *Human Biology* . **232** (3): 178. [doi](/wiki/Doi_(identifier) "Doi (identifier)"):[10.13110/humanbiology.90.3.01](https://doi.org/10.13110%2Fhumanbiology.90.3.01). [PMID](/wiki/PMID_(identifier) "PMID (identifier)") [33947174](https://pubmed.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/33947174). Retrieved September 11, 2020. Filipinos appear considerably admixed with respect to the other Asian population samples, carrying on average less Asian ancestry (71%) than our Korean (99%), Japanese (96%), Thai (93%), and Vietnamese (84%) reference samples. We also revealed substructure in our Filipino sample, showing that the patterns of ancestry vary within the Philippines---that is, between the four differently sourced Filipino samples. Mean estimates of Asian (76%) and European (7%) ancestry are greatest for the cemetery sample of forensic signifĳicance from Manila.{#cite_note-225}
{#cite_note-225}
224. **[\^](#cite_ref-226)** Go MC, Jones AR, Algee-Hewitt B, Dudzik B, Hughes C (2019). ["Classification Trends among Contemporary Filipino Crania Using Fordisc 3.1"](https://www.academia.edu/38744342). *Human Biology* . **2** (4). University of Florida Press: 1--11. [doi](/wiki/Doi_(identifier) "Doi (identifier)"):[10.5744/fa.2019.1005](https://doi.org/10.5744%2Ffa.2019.1005). [S2CID](/wiki/S2CID_(identifier) "S2CID (identifier)") [159266278](https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:159266278). Retrieved September 13, 2020. \[Page 1\] ABSTRACT: Filipinos represent a significant contemporary demographic group globally, yet they are underrepresented in the forensic anthropological literature. Given the complex population history of the Philippines, it is important to ensure that traditional methods for assessing the biological profile are appropriate when applied to these peoples. Here we analyze the classification trends of a modern Filipino sample (n = 110) when using the Fordisc 3.1 (FD3) software. We hypothesize that Filipinos represent an admixed population drawn largely from Asian and marginally from European parental gene pools, such that FD3 will classify these individuals morphometrically into reference samples that reflect a range of European admixture, in quantities from small to large. Our results show the greatest classification into Asian reference groups (72.7%), followed by Hispanic (12.7%), Indigenous American (7.3%), African (4.5%), and European (2.7%) groups included in FD3. This general pattern did not change between males and females. Moreover, replacing the raw craniometric values with their shape variables did not significantly alter the trends already observed. These classification trends for Filipino crania provide useful information for casework interpretation in forensic laboratory practice. Our findings can help biological anthropologists to better understand the evolutionary, population historical, and statistical reasons for FD3-generated classifications. The results of our studyindicate that ancestry estimation in forensic anthropology would benefit from population-focused research that gives consideration to histories of colonialism and periods of admixture.{#cite_note-226}
{#cite_note-226}

The cultural identity of the mestizos was challenged as they became increasingly aware that they were true members of neither the Indio nor the Chinese community. Increasingly powerful but adrift, they linked with the Spanish mestizos, who were also being challenged because after the Latin American revolutions broke the Spanish Empire, many of the settlers from the New World, Caucasian Creoles born in Mexico or Peru, became suspect in the eyes of the Iberian Spanish. The Spanish Empire had lost its universality.{#cite_note-229}

*[±% p.a.]: Per annum growth rate. Executive Order 135 §6 states that for "census years" (years divisible by 10) the reference date would be May 1st, but for all other years, the reference date is to be the "middle of the year". This means that growth rates, although correct, are not necessarily simple year-on-year comparisons.
